Wasiyyah — Bequest

8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Al-Jam' Al-Muhalla Bi Al-Lam in Bequests to Classes
Intra-Hanafi dispute on definite plural in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on interpreting al-jam' al-muhalla bi al-lam in wasiyyah and calculate the distribution of a bequest according to each view.

Core Idea
A definite plural in a bequest can indicate the genus, allowing one recipient; Muhammad requires at least two.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi debate on how to distribute a bequest made to a class of people like 'the poor' using a definite plural noun. The dispute hinges on whether the plural indicates the genus (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) or a minimum number of two (Muhammad). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly calculating shares in wills.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the two positions
Identify the bequest scenario (e.g., one-third to 'the poor') and note that Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf hold one recipient suffices, while Muhammad holds at least two are required.
The dispute is about the interpretation of the definite plural noun.
2
Identify the proof for each side
For lahuma: Quranic verse 'لَا يَحِلُّ لَكَ النِّسَاءُ' where plural is used for genus. For Muhammad: the maxim 'al-wasiyyah ukht al-mirath' and inheritance rules requiring minimum two.
The Quranic verse is a dalil naqli for the majority.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to Muhammad's argument
Evaluate why the majority rejects the inheritance analogy: the context of will is different, and the definite plural commonly indicates genus.
The response is based on linguistic principle and practicality.
4
Apply the dispute to numerical examples
Work through the examples: when bequest is to an individual and a class, calculate distribution under each view (e.g., 1/3 divided among 5 vs 7 shares).
Numerical difference illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical consequence
State that the relied-upon position is lahuma, so in practice one recipient per class suffices. This simplifies distribution.
The mufta bihi is based on majority view and Quranic usage.

Source Text

(٢) يعني بين زيد مثلا والمساكين، ويجوز صرف ما للمساكين لواحد منهم، وعند محمد يقسم الثلث يعني لزيد ثلثه وثلثاه للمساكين، ولا يجوز صرف ما للمساكين لأقل من اثنين عنده. ينظر : الشرنبلالية» (٤ : ٤٣٦). (٣) الأحزاب : ٥٢ . نصيب زيد وعمرو متساويان، وقد أُشْرَكَ آخر معهما ، فهو شريك للاثنين، فله ثلث ما لكل واحد منهما ، ولا يمكن مثل هذا في الصورة الثانية ؛ لتفاوتِ نصيب زيد وعمرو ، فهو شريك لكل واحد ، فله نصف لكل واحد منهما. (وفي له علي دين فصدِّقُوه صُدِّقَ إلى الثلث) : أي أمر أن يُصدِّقوا الدائن في مقدار الدين ، يجب عليهم أن يصدقوه إلى الثلث ، فأصل الحقِّ دين ، ومقداره يثبت بطريق الوصية، وهذا استحسان، وفي القياس لا يُصَدَّق ؛ لأنَّ المدعي لا يُصَدِّقُ إلا بحجة. ل : فَإِن كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِن ذَلِكَ فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ فِي الثُّلث ) ، فيستوي الذكور والإناث في الثلث. ففي الصورة الأولى نصيب زيد وعمرو متساويان وقد، أشرك آخر منهما فهو شريك للإثنين ، فله ثلث ما لكلِّ واحدٍ منهما ؛ لاتحاد المال، فللآخر يكون ثلاثمئة ، وهي ست وستون وثلثا درهم، كما لكل من زيد وعمرو. بخلاف الصورة الثانية ؛ لأنه لا يمكن مثل هذا التفاوت نصیب زيد وعمرو، فله نصف ما لكل واحد منهما، وهو خمس وسبعون ؛ لأنه كان لزيد مئة ونصفها خمسون، ولعمرو خمسون، ونصفها لا خمسة وعشرون ولزيد ولعمرو خمسة وعشرون درهما.
And one third for him, and half for the poor, for him and half for them, and one hundred for Zayd and one hundred for 'Amr, or with it for Zayd and fifty for 'Amr if he includes another with them, then he gets one third of what each has in the first case, and half of it in the second case. The word is plural, and its minimum in inheritance is two, and the will is the sister of inheritance. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): that the definite plural 'al-jam' al-muhalla bi al-lam' is intended for the genus, and the plural meaning is invalidated, like His saying: 'Women are not lawful for you', so it is intended for one, so it is divided into five, and they have three of them. ('And with one third for him, and half for the poor, for him and half for them') this is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa), and according to Muhammad, for him the third is divided into three parts. [1] ('And with one hundred for Zayd and one hundred for 'Amr, or with it for Zayd and fifty for 'Amr if he includes another with them, then he gets one third of what each has in the first case, and half of it in the second case') because in the first case, according to Muhammad: that what is mentioned is the word for the poor and the needy is plural, and its minimum in inheritance is two, we find that in the Quran, and the will is the sister of inheritance as mentioned, so for each group of the poor and the needy there are two, and for the mothers of children one third, so by considering the number of heads, the third is divided into seven shares. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa): that the definite plural 'al-jam' al-muhalla bi al-lam' is intended for the genus and the plural meaning is invalidated, like His saying 'Women are not lawful for you', so it is intended for one and the genus, it encompasses the minimum with the possibility of all, especially when it is impossible to refer it to all, so one from each group is considered, so the calculation reaches five, so the three are for the three, and the two are for the two. Thus it is understood from the expression of the commentary and some marginal notes of 'Al-Hidayah'. [11] His saying: 'And if he includes another with them', meaning by saying to another: 'I have included you with them in the two cases', then he gets one third of the whole, one in the first and half in the second, because partnership requires equality by His saying (Surah Al-Ahzab, verse 52). (2) Meaning between Zayd for example and the needy, and it is permissible to give what is for the needy to one of them, and according to Muhammad the third is divided into three parts for Zayd, one third is for Zayd and two thirds are for the needy, and it is not permissible to give what is for the needy to less than two according to him. See 'Al-Sharnablaliyyah' (4:436). (3) Al-Ahzab: 52. The share of Zayd and 'Amr are equal, and another has been included with them, so he is a partner for the two, so he gets one third of what each of them has, and such is not possible in the second case due to the disparity of Zayd and 'Amr's shares, so he is a partner for each, so he gets half of each of them. ('And if he owes a debt to someone, they should believe him, believed up to one third') meaning he ordered that they should believe the creditor in the amount of the debt, they must believe him up to one third, so the essence of the right is a debt, and its amount is established by way of will, and this is istihsan, and in qiyas he should not be believed because the claimant is not believed except with evidence. [...] So in the first case, the share of Zayd and 'Amr are equal, and another has been included with them, so he is a partner for the two, so he gets one third of what each of them has due to the unity of the property, so for the other there will be three hundred, which is sixty-six and two-thirds dirhams, as for each of Zayd and 'Amr. Unlike the second case, because such disparity of the share of Zayd and 'Amr is not possible, so he gets half of what each of them has, which is seventy-five, because for Zayd there was one hundred and its half is fifty, and for 'Amr fifty and its half is twenty-five, and for Zayd and 'Amr (?) twenty-five dirhams.
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage addresses the distribution of bequests made to groups of people (e.g., the poor and the needy) and the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding how to count the recipients. The text presents two key rulings: first, when a testator leaves one-third to a specific individual and half to the poor, the third is divided between the individual and the poor; second, when leaving specific money amounts to named individuals and including a partner, the partner's share depends on whether the original shares were equal or unequal. The core controversy centers on the interpretation of the definite plural (al-jam' al-muhalla bi al-lam) in the phrase 'the poor'—whether it indicates the minimum plural of two (Muhammad's view, linking to inheritance rules) or the genus/species with the plural meaning nullified (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's view, citing Quranic usage 'Women are not lawful for you' where the plural refers to any one woman). This disagreement affects the distribution: Muhammad requires at least two recipients from each group, while the other two consider one sufficient. The text also illustrates the application with numbers: in the first case, equal shares of 100 for Zayd and 'Amr, a new partner gets 1/3 of each (i.e., 33.33 each, total 66.66); in the second case, unequal shares (100 and 50), the partner gets half of each (50 from Zayd, 25 from 'Amr, total 75). The ruling is an expansion (sharh) of the base matn, using Quranic verse as proof (dalil naqli) and clarifying the positions of the three Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf (their view is 'lahuma'), and Muhammad.

Key Terms
الجمع المحلى باللام (al-jam' al-muhalla bi al-lam): A plural noun prefixed with the definite article 'al-', which in this context is argued to indicate the genus rather than a specific number of individuals.
الوصية أخت الميراث (al-wasiyyah ukht al-mirath): A maxim meaning that the rules of will (wasiyyah) are analogous to the rules of inheritance (mirath) in certain aspects, such as the minimum number for a plural.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, how many individuals are needed from a class like 'the poor' when a bequest is made to them using a definite plural?
A) At least two
B) At least three
C) One individual suffices
D) The number must be specifically stated

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a definite plural noun in a bequest is interpreted as genus, so one recipient suffices, though Muhammad disagreed.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Acknowledgment of Debt by a Dying Person: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling on believing a dying person's claim of debt up to one-third of the estate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school uses istihsan to override qiyas in the case of a dying person's acknowledgment of debt and state the resulting ruling that heirs must believe the creditor up to one-third of the estate.

Core Idea
A dying person's acknowledgment of debt is treated as a will by istihsan, binding heirs up to one-third.

Imagine a person on their deathbed tells their heirs, 'I owe Zayd 500 dirhams,' but no proof exists. Should the heirs pay Zayd? Strict legal analogy (qiyas) says no, because claimants need evidence. However, Hanafi law applies istihsan—juristic preference—to treat the acknowledgment as a will, valid within the one-third limit. This lesson unpacks that reasoning, revealing the role of istihsan in giving effect to the testator's intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is the dying person's instruction to heirs to 'believe' a creditor regarding the amount of debt. The ruling: the heirs must (wajib) accept the claim up to one-third of the estate.
The obligation is limited to one-third because the acknowledgment is treated as a bequest (wasiyyah) by istihsan.
2
Locate the Proof
No textual proof (Qur'an/Hadith) is cited. The ruling is based on istihsan, a rational preference that overrides qiyas. Istihsan derives from the testator's intent to prioritize the creditor and the flexibility to treat the acknowledgment as a will.
Istihsan is a distinct Hanafi source, not accepted by all schools.
3
Understand the Qiyas Counterargument
The default rule (qiyas) is that a claimant is not believed without evidence (al-mudda'i la yusaddaqu illa bi hujjah). Since the creditor has no proof, the claim should be rejected entirely.
Qiyas here is jaliyy (clear analogy), but istihsan overrides it.
4
Analyze the Istihsan Argument
Istihsan considers the dying person's known goal: to give the creditor priority over heirs. This goal can be achieved by treating the acknowledgment as a will (wasiyyah), which is valid up to one-third. The testator's insistence on 'belief' indicates he desires the debt to be honored despite lack of proof.
The amount is left to the creditor's claim, as if the testator said, 'When he comes to you, believe him.'
5
Determine the Cross-Madhab Impact
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school due to istihsan. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not recognize istihsan as a formal source and would likely require evidence for the debt, rejecting the claim if unproven.
The practical difference: Hanafis protect the creditor's claim up to one-third; others may deny it entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي له علي دين فصدِّقُوه صُدِّقَ إلى الثلث: أي أمر أن يُصدِّقوا الدائن في مقدار الدين ، يجب عليهم أن يصدقوه إلى الثلث ، فأصل الحقِّ دين ، ومقداره يثبت بطريق الوصية، وهذا استحسان، وفي القياس لا يُصَدَّق ؛ لأنَّ المدعي لا يُصَدِّقُ إلا بحجة. ووجه الاستحسان : أنا نعلمُ أنّ من قصدِهِ تقديمه على الورثة، وقد أمكن تنفيذ قصده بطريق الوصية، وقد يحتاجُ إليه من يعلمُ بأصل الحق عليه دون مقداره سعياً منه في تفريغ ذمته، فبجعلها وصيّة جعل التقدير فيها إلى الموصي له ، كأنه قال : إذا جاءكم
And if he owes a debt to someone, then believe him, believed up to one third: meaning he ordered that they should believe the creditor in the amount of the debt, they must believe him up to one third, so the essence of the right is a debt, and its amount is established by way of will, and this is istihsan, and in qiyas he should not be believed because the claimant is not believed except with evidence. The basis of istihsan: we know that his intention is to give him priority over the heirs, and it is possible to execute his intention by way of will, and it may be needed by someone who knows the existence of the right upon him but not its amount, in his effort to free his conscience, so by making it a will, the estimation is given to the legatee, as if he said: When he comes to you...
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage deals with a dying person's acknowledgment of a debt to a third party. The testator instructs the heirs to 'believe him' (the creditor) regarding the amount of the debt. The ruling is that the heirs must accept the creditor's claim up to one-third of the estate, treating the excess as a bequest (wasiyyah). This is a ruling based on istihsan (juristic preference) contradicting qiyas (analogy). In qiyas, the normal rule would apply: a claimant is not believed without proof, and since the dying person's acknowledgment is essentially a claim without evidence, it would be rejected. However, istihsan recognizes the dying person's intent to benefit the creditor and allows the acknowledgment to be treated as a will (wasiyyah), which is permissible up to one-third of the estate. The reasoning is that the dying person's purpose is to give the creditor priority over the heirs, and this can be achieved by considering the acknowledgment as a bequest. Moreover, the person may know the existence of the debt but not its exact amount, and he wants to clear his liability. Thus, the estimation of the amount is left to the legatee (the creditor), as if the testator said, 'When he comes to you, believe him.'

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that allows deviating from strict analogy (qiyas) for a more equitable or practical ruling. Here, it is used to accept the creditor's claim despite lack of evidence.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will that takes effect after death, valid only up to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do the heirs have to believe the creditor's claim of debt up to one-third according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the creditor has proof
B) Because of istihsan, treating it as a will
C) Because it is a clear Quranic command
D) Because the heirs must always believe the dying person

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to treat a dying person's debt acknowledgment as a will, binding heirs to pay up to one-third of the estate even without proof.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

Bequest with Debt: Allocation and Oath Procedure
Ruling on bequest with debt allocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi procedure for allocating bequest and inheritance when a debt is claimed, including the acknowledgment and oath requirements.

Core Idea
A known bequest and inheritance are set aside first; an unknown debt is resolved by acknowledgment and oath from legatees and heirs.

When a testator makes a bequest and a debt is also claimed, the known rights of the bequest (one-third) and inheritance (two-thirds) are set aside first. However, the debt is unknown and must be determined through acknowledgment by both parties, followed by an oath that they know of no increase. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind this procedure from the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Problem
Recognize that the estate has two known allocations (bequest and inheritance) and an unknown debt claim. The procedure must preserve the known shares while resolving the unknown debt.
2
Understand the Allocation Order
The one-third for bequest and two-thirds for inheritance are set aside first because they are known. The debt claim, being unknown, does not compete directly with these fixed shares.
This is based on the principle that known rights are not disturbed by unknown claims.
3
Learn the Acknowledgment Process
Both legatees and heirs are asked to acknowledge whatever they wish regarding the debt claim. This acknowledgment determines the amount of debt for each party's share.
The debt is taken proportionally from the shares based on what each party acknowledged.
4
Examine the Oath Requirement
Each party must swear that they have no knowledge of an increase beyond what was claimed. This oath is necessary because the claim involves knowledge of transactions between the deceased and the claimant.
The oath is on knowledge ('ilm), not on the act itself, making it a unique procedural element.
5
Trace the Commentary Expansion
Follow how the commentary (from al-Hidayah and al-Durr al-Mukhtar) expands the base text: it explains why the known shares are prioritized, why the debt is treated as unknown, and how the oath resolves the doubt.
This expansion is typical of Hanafi legal commentaries that provide ratio legis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن أوصى مع ذلك عُزل ثلث لها ، وثلثاه للورثة ، وقيل لكل : صدقوه فيما شئتم ، ويؤخذ ذو الثلث بثلث ما أقروا به، وما بقي فلهم، والورثة بثلثي ما أقروا به ، ويَحْلِفُ كل على العلم بدعوى الزيادة (أي أوصى مع ذلك الدين الذي أمر بتصديق مقدارِهِ بثُلُثِ مالهِ لقوم ، يُعْزَلُ ثُلُثُ المال للوصية والثلثان للورثة ، وقيل للموصى لهم صدّقوه فيما شئتم ، فإذا أقروا بمقدار فقُلتُ ذلك المقدار يكون في حقهم، وهو ثلث المال، وما بقى من الثُّلُثِ فللموصَى لهم. فلان وادَّعى شيئاً فأعطوه من مالي ما شاء، وهذه معتبرة من الثلث ؛ فلهذا يصدق على الثلث دون الزيادة. كذا في «الهداية»). قوله : عزل ثلث لها ... الخ؛ لأنَّ الوصايا حقوق معلومة في الثلث، والميراث معلوم في الثلثين، وهذا الإقرار ليس بدين معلوم ولا وصيّة معلومة، فلا يزاحم المعلوم، فقدمنا عزل المعلوم. كذا في «الرد المحتار) ناقلاً عن الزيلعي. قوله : فلهم ؛ أي للموصى لهم، فإن قيل : قوله : لفلان علي دين، فصدقوه إقرار بدين، والدين مقدم على حق الورثة ، وحق أصحاب الوصايا ، فَلِمَ قدم العزل لهما عليه. قلنا : الدين إن كان مقدَّماً على الحقين إلا أنه مجهول، وطريق تعينه ما ذكر من تصديق الفريقين. قوله : بثلثي ما أقروا به ؛ لأنه إذا أقرّ كلّ فريق بسهم ظهر أنّ في التركةِ ديناً شائعاً في النصيبين، فيؤخذ الدين منهم بحساب ما في أيديهم من التركة. كذا في «الردّ المحتار) ناقلا عن العينيه وغيره. قوله : فللموصى لهم ؛ حتى لو قال : الموصى لهم الدين مئة ، يعطى المقر له ثلثها مما في أيديهم، فإن فضل شيءٌ فلهم، وإلا فلا. كذا في «الردّ المحتار).
If he bequeaths along with that, one-third is set aside for it, and two-thirds for the heirs; and it is said to each: believe him regarding what you wish. The one with the third is taken with one-third of what they acknowledged, and the remainder is for them; the heirs are taken with two-thirds of what they acknowledged; and each swears regarding knowledge of the claim of increase. That is, if he bequeaths along with that debt which he ordered to be verified of its amount with one-third of his property to a group, one-third of the property is set aside for the bequest and two-thirds for the heirs; and it is said to the legatees: believe him regarding what you wish; when they acknowledge an amount, then that amount is in their right, and it is one-third of the property, and what remains from the third is for the legatees. So-and-so claims something, so give him from my property what he wishes, and this is considered from the third; therefore he is believed regarding the third, not beyond it. Thus in al-Hidayah. His statement: 'set aside one-third for it' etc.; because bequests are known rights in the third, and inheritance is known in the two-thirds, and this acknowledgment is neither a known debt nor a known bequest, so it does not compete with the known, so we prioritize setting aside the known. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, quoting al-Zayla'i. His statement: 'the remainder is for them' i.e., for the legatees. It might be said: his statement 'to so-and-so I owe a debt, they confirmed it' is an acknowledgment of a debt, and the debt is prioritized over the right of the heirs and the right of the legatees; why then did he prioritize setting aside for them? We say: the debt, although prioritized over the two rights, is unknown, and the way to determine it is what was mentioned of the two groups' confirmation. His statement: 'with two-thirds of what they acknowledged'; because when each group acknowledges a portion, it appears that there is a general debt in the two shares, so the debt is taken from them according to what is in their hands of the estate. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar quoting al-Ayni and others. His statement: 'and the remainder is for the legatees'; so if the legatees say the debt is one hundred, the acknowledged person is given one-third of that from what is in their hands; if anything remains, it is for them, otherwise not. Thus in al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_statement and expansion from the commentary on a matn. It deals with the scenario where a person makes a bequest (wasiyyah) while also having a debt (dayn). The initial ruling is clear: one-third of the estate is set aside for the bequest, and two-thirds for the heirs. However, when there is an additional claim (e.g., the legatee or a creditor alleges a debt against the deceased), the text instructs that each party (legatees and heirs) should be asked to acknowledge whatever they wish regarding the debt. Then, the one who is entitled to the third (the legatee) receives one-third of what they acknowledged, and the remainder of the third goes to the legatees; the heirs receive two-thirds of what they acknowledged. Additionally, each party must swear that they have no knowledge of an increase beyond what was claimed. The commentary explains the rationale: bequests and inheritance are known rights in fixed shares, but the acknowledgment is not a known debt or known bequest, so it does not disturb the known shares. The debt, although generally prioritized over bequests and inheritance, is unknown here, so its determination depends on the acknowledgment of both groups. The oath is necessary because the claim of increase involves knowledge of what occurred between the deceased and the claimant, not a direct action of the swearer.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest made by a testator for someone other than an heir, valid only up to one-third of the estate.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum amount a testator can bequeath without heirs' consent.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right or debt by a party, here the legatees and heirs acknowledging the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a bequest along with a debt, what must each party (legatees and heirs) do regarding the debt claim?
A) They must pay the debt immediately from their shares.
B) They must acknowledge what they wish and swear they know of no increase.
C) They must ignore the debt and distribute as per the will.
D) They must call the creditor to prove the debt.

Key Takeaway
When a bequest and an unknown debt coexist, known shares are set aside first, and the debt is resolved through proportional acknowledgment and an oath on knowledge of increase.

Half for the Stranger: Bequest to Heir and Non-Heir
Ruling on joint bequest to an heir and stranger

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a testator bequeaths a specific item jointly to an heir and a stranger, and explain the reasoning behind the distinction from a bequest to a living and a dead person.

Core Idea
A bequest to an heir is void without consent, so the stranger takes half and the heir takes nothing.

This lesson examines a scenario where a testator bequeaths a specific thing jointly to an heir and a stranger. The Hanafi ruling is clear: the stranger receives half of that thing, and the heir receives nothing because the bequest to an heir is void unless the other heirs consent. The commentary draws a contrast with a bequest to a living and a dead person to highlight the difference in capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
The testator bequeaths a specific item to both an heir (e.g., son) and a non-heir (stranger).
This is a single bequest with two beneficiaries.
2
State the ruling for each
Stranger gets half the item; heir gets nothing because his share is void.
The text says 'khaba al-warith' meaning the heir's hope is cut off.
3
Understand the reasoning
The heir is capable of receiving a bequest (ahlun lil-wasiyyah), so the invalidity arises from prohibition, not incapacity. In contrast, a dead person is not capable.
The analogy to bequest to a living and dead person shows that incapacity gives the entire item to the capable.
4
Apply the same rule to the killer
If he bequeaths to a killer and a stranger, the stranger gets half, and the killer's share becomes invalid.
The text is cut off but indicates the same ruling applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعين لوارث وأجنبي، له نصف، وخاب الوارث (أي إن أوصى بشيء معين لوارث وأجنبي، فللأجنبي نصف ذلك الشيء، وخاب الوارث : أي قطع الرجاء من الوصية؛ لبطلانها في حقه، وإنما يكون النصف للأجنبي؛ لأنَّ الوارث أهل الوصية: أي يصلح أن يكون مالكاً. بخلاف ما إذا أوصى به للحي والميت، حيث يكون كل الوصية للحي؛ لأنَّ الميت ليس بأهل للوصية فلا يصلح أن يكون مزاحماً للحي، والوارث من أهلها، ولهذا تصح الوصية للوارث بإجازة الورثة. وعلى هذا إذا أوصى للقاتل والأجنبي؛ فللأجنبي نصف الوصية، وتبطل
And if he bequeaths a specific thing to an heir and a stranger, the stranger gets half, and the heir fails (i.e., his hope is cut off from the bequest due to its invalidity in his right). Half is only for the stranger because the heir is capable of receiving a bequest (i.e., he can be the owner). Unlike if he bequeaths it to a living person and a dead person, where the entire bequest goes to the living because the dead is not capable of receiving a bequest and thus cannot compete with the living. The heir is among those capable, and therefore the bequest to an heir becomes valid with the consent of the other heirs. Similarly, if he bequeaths to a killer and a stranger, the stranger gets half the bequest, and it becomes invalid
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This is a ruling_statement and expansion from the commentary. It addresses a scenario where a testator bequeaths a specific item to both an heir (e.g., his son) and a stranger (non-heir) jointly. The ruling is that the stranger receives half of that item, and the heir receives nothing—his hope is disappointed because the bequest to an heir is invalid without the consent of the other heirs. The commentary explains the reasoning: the heir is legally capable of receiving a bequest (i.e., he can be the owner), so the invalidity is not due to incapacity but to the prohibition against bequeathing to heirs unless consented. In contrast, if the bequest were to a living person and a dead person, the dead person's share becomes invalid due to lack of capacity, so the living receives the entire item. The same analogy is applied to a bequest to a killer (who is disqualified from inheritance by killing) and a stranger: the stranger gets half, and the killer's share becomes invalid.

Key Terms
الوارث (al-warith): An heir who inherits from the deceased by law.
الأجنبي (al-ajnabi): A person who is not an heir of the deceased, eligible to receive a bequest up to one-third.
خاب (khaba): To fail or be disappointed; here, the heir's hope of receiving the bequest is cut off.
أهل الوصية (ahl al-wasiyyah): Capable of receiving a bequest, i.e., legally competent to own property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The son gets the car and the friend gets nothing.
B) The friend gets the whole car because the son's share is void.
C) The friend gets half the car and the son gets the other half.
D) The friend gets half the car and the son gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to an heir is void unless consented to by other heirs; the stranger's share is valid only for half of the specified item when bequeathed jointly.

Bequest to an Heir and a Non-Heir: Hanafi Ruling and Reasoning
Ruling on bequest to heir and non-heir with reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a bequest to both an heir and a non-heir, explain why the non-heir receives half, and distinguish this from an acknowledgment (iqrar).

Core Idea
A bequest to an heir is void without other heirs' consent; to a non-heir it is valid. In a joint bequest, the non-heir takes half, the heir gets nothing.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi wasiyya law: what happens when a testator bequeaths a specific item to both an heir and a non-heir. The text from the Book of Bequests, based on the matn of Al-Quduri and its sharḥ, provides the ruling and its underlying reasoning (taʿlīl). By understanding this case, you will grasp the fundamental distinction between bequests to heirs and non-heirs in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The case involves a testator who bequeaths a specific item (e.g., a house) to two persons: one is an heir (warith) and the other is a non-heir (ajnabī).
The text assumes the bequest is of a specific 'ayn (specific item), not a portion of the estate.
2
State the ruling
The non-heir receives half of that item, while the heir gets nothing (the heir is 'disappointed'). The bequest to the heir is invalid (bāṭil) unless the other heirs consent after death.
This is the muftā bihī position in the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the reasoning (taʿlīl)
The heir is 'eligible for bequest' (ahl al-waṣiyya), i.e., capable of being a legatee. Because he is eligible, the bequest is split between him and the stranger; but since the heir's portion is void (due to lack of consent), the stranger's half remains valid. This differs from bequest to a living and a dead person: the dead is not eligible, so the entire bequest goes to the living.
The key phrase: 'because the heir is qualified' (li-anna al-wāritha ahl al-waṣiyya).
4
Apply the analogy
The same rule applies if the testator bequeaths to a killer (qātil) and a stranger: the stranger gets half, the killer's share is invalid. Also, if the testator acknowledges (iqrār) a specific item or debt to both an heir and a stranger, the acknowledgment is invalid for both—unlike the bequest case.
The distinction between wasiyya and iqrār is critical: iqrār is a legal admission that binds the testator before death, whereas wasiyya takes effect after death and is subject to the one-third rule.
5
Analyze the heirs' confirmation and oath
If the heirs confirm a claim (e.g., a debt or bequest) against the estate, the claimant receives two-thirds of the confirmed amount. Each party (legatee and heirs) must swear that they do not know of any excess claim. The oath is on knowledge (ʿalā al-ʿilm), not certainty, because it concerns the actions of the deceased.
This part integrates procedural rules into the substantive law of bequests.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا / تعريفها وأحكامها

وبعين لوارث وأجنبي، له نصف، وخاب الوارث

ويقال للورثة : صدقوه فيما شئتم، فإذا أقروا بشيء، فثلثا ذلك الشيء يكون في حقهم، وهو ثلثا المال، والباقي للورثة ، وحَلَف كل واحد من الموصى له والورثة على العلم بدعوى الزيادة".

( وبعين لوارث ) وأجنبي، له نصف، وخاب الوارث)، وإنما يكونُ للأجنبي النصف ؛ لأنَّ الوارث أهلُ الوصية بخلاف ما إذا أوصى به للحي والميت، فإن الميت ليس بأهل. [۱] قوله : والباقي للورثة ؛ حتى لو قال الورثة : الدين ثلاثمئة، يعطى المقر له مئتين مما في أيديهم، فإن فضل شيءٌ فلهم، وإلا فلا. كذا في رد المحتار) ناقلاً عن الإتقاني .

[٢]قوله : على العلم ؛ أي بأنهم لا يعلمون أنه أكثر من ذلك ؛ لأنه تحليف على فعل الغير أي على ما جرى بين المدعي والميت، لا على فعل نفسه، فلا يحلف على البتات. كذا في الرد المحتار) [٣] قوله : بدعوى الزيادة ؛ إشارة إلى اشتراط لزوم اليمين ؛ لوجودِ الدعوى كما لا يخفى على المتأمل.

(۲)

[٤] قوله : وبعين الوارث... الخ ؛ أي إن أوصى بشيء معين لوارث وأجنبي، فللأجنبي نصف ذلك الشيء، وخاب الوارث : أي قطع الرجاء من الوصية ؛ لبطلانها في حقه، وإنما يكون النصف للأجنبي ؛ لأنَّ الوارث أهل الوصية : أي يصلح أن يكون مالكاً.

بخلاف ما إذا أوصى به للحي والميت، حيث يكون كل الوصية للحي ؛ لأنَّ الميت ليس بأهل للوصية فلا يصلح أن يكون مزاحماً للحي، والوارث من أهلها، ولهذا تصح الوصية للوارث بإجازة الورثة.

وعلى هذا إذا أوصى للقاتل والأجنبي ؛ فللأجنبي نصف الوصية ، وتبطل الوصية للقاتل، وهذا بخلاف ما إذا أقر بعين أو دين لوارثه، وللأجنبي حيث لا يصح في حق الأجنبي أيضاً، كما لا يصح في حق الوارث. كذا في الشروح.
Book of Bequests / Its Definition and Rulings. And with a specific thing to an heir and a non-relative (stranger), he (the stranger) gets half, and the heir is disappointed. And it is said to the heirs: Confirm him in whatever you wish; if they admit something, then two-thirds of that thing is for them, and it is two-thirds of the estate, and the remainder is for the heirs; and each of the legatee and the heirs takes an oath concerning knowledge of the claim of excess. (And with a specific thing to an heir and a stranger, he gets half, and the heir is disappointed). And the stranger only gets half because the heir is qualified for bequest, unlike if he bequeaths it to a living person and a dead person, for the dead person is not qualified. [1] His statement: 'and the remainder is for the heirs'; such that if the heirs say: the debt is three hundred, the one acknowledged is given two hundred from what is in their hands; if anything extra remains, it is for them, otherwise not. Quoted from Radd al-Muhtar, transmitted from al-Itqani. [2] His statement: 'concerning knowledge'; i.e., that they do not know that it is more than that, because it is an oath about the action of another, i.e., about what occurred between the claimant and the deceased, not about his own action, so he does not swear definitely. Quoted from Radd al-Muhtar. [3] His statement: 'of the claim of excess'; an indication of the condition of necessity of the oath due to the existence of the claim, as is not hidden from the contemplative. (2) [4] His statement: 'and with a specific thing to an heir...' i.e., if he bequeaths a specific thing to an heir and a stranger, then the stranger gets half of that thing, and the heir is disappointed: i.e., cut off from hope of the bequest because it is invalid in his right; and the half is only for the stranger because the heir is qualified for bequest, i.e., he is fit to be an owner. Unlike if he bequeaths it to a living person and a dead person, where the entire bequest is for the living because the dead is not qualified for bequest and is not fit to compete with the living; and the heir is among those qualified, and therefore the bequest to an heir is valid with the consent of the heirs. And upon this, if he bequeaths to the killer and a stranger, then the stranger gets half the bequest, and the bequest to the killer is invalid; and this is unlike if he acknowledges a specific thing or a debt to his heir and to a stranger, where it is not valid with respect to the stranger either, just as it is not valid with respect to the heir. Thus in the commentaries.
Source pages p. 605

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Bequests contains two related rulings. First, the ruling on a bequest of a specific item to both an heir and a non-heir (ajnabi). The base text (matn) states that the non-heir takes half of the item and the heir gets nothing. The commentary explains that the non-heir receives half because the heir is 'qualified for bequest' (ahl al-wasiyya), meaning he is capable of being a legatee, but his portion is automatically invalid unless the other heirs consent. By contrast, if a bequest were made to a living person and a dead person, the entire bequest goes to the living because the dead is not qualified. The analogy extends to a bequest to a killer (qatil) and a stranger: the stranger takes half and the killer's share is invalid. The second part addresses what happens when heirs confirm or deny a claim (e.g., a debt or bequest) made against the estate. The heirs are told to either confirm or deny; if they confirm a certain amount, the claimant receives two-thirds of that amount (which is two-thirds of the entire estate if the claim is the estate itself), and the remaining one-third stays with the heirs. They must swear that they do not know of any excess claim. The oath is on knowledge, not certainty, because it concerns the actions of the deceased. The commentary adds that if the heirs say the debt is 300, the claimant gets 200 from what is in their hands. Finally, a distinction is made between bequest and acknowledgment (iqrar): if a testator acknowledges a specific item or debt to both an heir and a stranger, the acknowledgment is invalid for both, contrary to the case of bequest where the stranger's share is valid.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest or testamentary disposition of property after death, valid up to one-third of the estate without consent of heirs.
وارث (warith): An heir entitled to a share of the estate by inheritance.
أجنبي (ajnabi): A non-heir, a person not entitled to inherit from the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The entire painting
B) Half of the painting
C) One-third of the painting
D) Nothing, because the bequest is invalid due to the daughter's share

Key Takeaway
In a joint bequest to an heir and a non-heir, the non-heir receives half of the specific item, and the heir receives nothing from that bequest.

Distribution When a Bequeathed Garment Is Lost
Ruling on distribution when a bequeathed garment is lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for distributing remaining bequeathed items when one is lost and the specific entitlement is unknown, identifying the shares for each legatee.

Core Idea
Uncertainty about lost bequeathed items can be resolved by a proportional distribution when heirs consent.

Imagine a testator leaves three garments of different qualities—good, medium, poor—to three named individuals. After death, one garment is lost and no one knows which. The heirs initially say the bequest is invalid. But if they voluntarily surrender the remaining two garments, a specific division saves the bequest. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on this scenario, showing how legal reasoning resolves uncertainty in bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and Initial Ruling
The passage states that if one of three bequeathed garments is lost and its identity unknown, the bequest becomes invalid due to ignorance of the specific subject matter (jahalat al-mustahaqq).
This invalidity is not absolute; it is a temporary impediment.
2
Understand the Heirs' Role
The heirs declare that each legatee's right is lost. However, if the heirs voluntarily surrender the two remaining garments, the bequest becomes executable. This consent removes the impediment to delivery, not the impediment to validity.
The impediment to validity (ignorance) remains, but the impediment to delivery (heirs' repudiation) is removed.
3
Analyze the Distribution Formula
The person entitled to the good garment gets two-thirds of the better remaining garment; the person entitled to the inferior gets two-thirds of the inferior remaining; the person entitled to the middle gets one-third of each remaining garment.
This division is based on the probability of each legatee's entitlement to each specific garment.
4
Trace the Legal Reasoning (Talil)
The commentary explains: the middle person's right could be in either remaining garment depending on which was lost (if lost is the best, his right is in the inferior; if lost is the worst, his right is in the good; if lost is the middle, he has no right in either). Thus his right attaches to each in one scenario but not in two, so he takes one-third of each. The good and inferior claimants have no claim on the opposite garment, so they receive two-thirds of their respective garments.
This is a juristic solution (istihsan) to avoid total loss, supported by later Hanafi authorities.
5
Confirm the Source Authority
The ruling is quoted from Radd al-Muhtar and Sharh al-Jami' al-Khani, representing the later Hanafi (mutakhkhirin) tradition. It is the mufta bihi position.
Not from Zahir al-Riwayah, but accepted in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( وبثلاثة أثواب متفاوتة لكل لرجل إن ضاعَ ثوب ولم يدر أي هو، والورثة تقول : لكل تَوَى حقك بطلت ، لكن إن سلموا ما بقي "" أخذ ذو الجيد ثلثي الأعز، وذو الردئ ثلثي الاخس، وذو المتوسط ثلث كل) : أي أوصى بثلاثة أثواب متفاوتة : جيد، ومتوسط ، ورديء ، وقال : الجيد لزيد، والمتوسط لعمرو، والرديء لبكر، فَهَلَكَ واحد ولا يدرى أي هو ، والورثة تقولُ : لكلِّ واحدٍ هَلَكَ حقك، فالوصية باطلة، لكن الورثة إن تسامحوا وسلموا الثوبين الباقيين إلى زيد وعمرو وبكر، أخذ زيد ثلثي الأجود من الثّوبين، وأخذ بكر ثلثي الرديء، وعمر و ثُلُثَ كُلِّ واحد.

الوصية للقاتل، وهذا بخلاف ما إذا أقر بعين أو دين لوارثه، وللأجنبي حيث لا يصح في حق الأجنبي أيضاً، كما لا يصح في حق الوارث. كذا في الشروح. [ 1 ] قوله : بطلت ؛ لجهالة المستحق : أي الموصى له كوصية لأحد هذين الرجلين. (۲) قوله : لكن إن سلّموا ما بقي ؛ من الأثواب الثلاثة فتعود صحيحة لزوال المانع من التسليم، لا المانع من الصحة ؛ لأنَّ المانع منهما الجهالة، وهي باقية، والمانع من التسليم هو الجحود ؛ أي جحود الورثة بقاء حقٌّ كلّ، فتقسم بأن يأخذ ذو الجيد ؛ أي الجيد في نفس الأمر ثلثي الأعز إلى الجيد... الخ. ووجه هذه القسمة : أنّ ذا الوسط حقه في الجيد من الباقيين إن كان الهالك أرفع منهما ، وإن كان أردأ منهما فحقه في الرديء منهما ، فتعلّق حقه مرّة بهذا ومرة بالآخر، وإن كان الهالك هو الوسط فلا حق له فيهما.

فقد تعلق حقه بكلِّ واحدٍ من الباقين في حال ولم يتعلق في الحالين، فيأخذ ثلث كل منهما، وذو الجيد مدعي الجيد منهما لا الرديء، إذ لا حق لـه فـيه قطعاً، وذو الرديء يدعي الرديء لا الجيّد، فيُسَلَّمُ ثلثا الجيّد لذي الجيد، وثلثا الرديء لذي الرديء. هكذا ذكر صاحب رد المحتار (۱) ناقلاً عن «شرح الجامع الخاني».
(And with three garments of varying quality for each man: if a garment is lost and it is not known which it is, and the heirs say: for each one his right is lost, the bequest is invalid, but if they surrender what remains, the one entitled to the good takes two-thirds of the better one, the one entitled to the inferior takes two-thirds of the inferior, and the one entitled to the middle takes one-third of each). That is, he bequeathed three garments of varying quality: good, medium, and inferior, and said: the good is for Zayd, the medium for 'Amr, and the inferior for Bakr. One was lost and it is not known which, and the heirs say: for each one his right is lost, so the bequest is invalid. But if the heirs are magnanimous and surrender the two remaining garments to Zayd, 'Amr, and Bakr, then Zayd takes two-thirds of the better of the two garments, Bakr takes two-thirds of the inferior, and 'Amr takes one-third of each. The bequest to the killer, and this is unlike if he acknowledges a specific thing or debt to his heir and to a stranger, where it is not valid with respect to the stranger either, just as it is not valid with respect to the heir. Thus in the commentaries. [1] His statement: 'it is invalid' due to ignorance of the entitled person, i.e., the legatee, like a bequest to one of these two men. (2) His statement: 'but if they surrender what remains' of the three garments, then it becomes valid due to removal of the impediment to delivery, not the impediment to validity; because the impediment to both is ignorance, and it remains, and the impediment to delivery is repudiation, i.e., the heirs' repudiation of each one's right. So the division is such that the person entitled to the good (i.e., the good in reality) takes two-thirds of the better of the two, and so on. The basis of this division is that the one entitled to the middle has his right in the good of the remaining if the lost one is higher than both, and if it is lower than both, his right is in the inferior of the remaining; so his right attaches sometimes to this and sometimes to that; and if the lost one is the middle, he has no right in either. Thus his right attached to each of the remaining in one scenario and did not attach in two scenarios, so he takes one-third of each. The one entitled to the good claims the good of the two, not the inferior, as he has no right in it definitively; and the one entitled to the inferior claims the inferior, not the good. So two-thirds of the good is given to the one entitled to the good, and two-thirds of the inferior to the one entitled to the inferior. Thus mentioned the author of Radd al-Muhtar, quoting from Sharh al-Jami' al-Khani.
Source pages p. 606

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific scenario in bequests: a testator bequeaths three distinct garments of different qualities (good, medium, poor) to three named individuals. After the testator's death, one garment is lost and it is unknown which one is missing. The heirs initially claim that due to the uncertainty, the bequest is invalid for all. However, if the heirs voluntarily surrender the two remaining garments to the three legatees, a specific distribution is made: the person who was to receive the good garment takes two-thirds of the better of the two remaining garments; the one designated for the inferior takes two-thirds of the inferior; and the one designated for the middle takes one-third of each. The commentary explains the reasoning: the middle person's right could be in either of the remaining garments depending on which was lost, so he takes a share in both. The one for the good only claims the better one, and the one for the inferior only claims the worse one, so they receive two-thirds of their respective claimants. The initial invalidity is due to ignorance of the specific garment each legatee is entitled to, but when the heirs consent to deliver the remaining garments, the impediment to delivery is removed, not the impediment to validity (which remains due to ignorance). The distribution is a juristic solution to avoid total loss. This ruling is from the later Hanafi tradition, as quoted from Radd al-Muhtar and Sharh al-Jami' al-Khani.

Key Terms
أثواب متفاوتة (athwab mutafawwita): Garments of varying quality (good, medium, poor) bequeathed to different persons.
جهالة المستحق (jahalat al-mustahaqq): Ignorance of who is entitled to which specific garment, causing initial invalidity of the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of three bequeathed garments of different qualities with one lost, if the heirs surrender the remaining two, how much does the person designated for the middle garment receive?
A) Two-thirds of the better garment
B) The entire better garment
C) One-third of each of the two remaining garments
D) Nothing, because his entitlement is uncertain

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, uncertainty in a bequest due to loss of an item can be partially remedied by a proportional distribution when heirs consent, preserving the testator's intent.

Bequest of Three Different Garments When One Is Lost
Ruling and division formula for uncertain bequest of three garments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a bequest of specific items of different quality becomes uncertain due to loss, and apply the division formula when heirs concede.

Core Idea
Uncertainty invalidates a bequest, but heirs' consent can restore it with a prescribed proportional division.

When a testator bequeaths specific items of different quality to named legatees, the loss of one item creates uncertainty. The heirs may claim the bequest is void. However, Hanafi law provides a remedy: if the heirs voluntarily surrender the remaining items, a specific division resolves the uncertainty. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
A testator bequeaths three garments of different quality (good, medium, inferior) to three specific legatees. One garment is lost and it is unknown which one. This creates ignorance (jahāla) about which legatee's right has perished.
The heirs argue that the bequest is invalid because each legatee's claim is uncertain.
2
Understand the heirs' objection
The heirs say 'for each, your right has perished' (بطلت), meaning the bequest is void due to jahāla. The impediment is the uncertainty of entitlement.
Jahāla regarding the legatee or subject matter normally invalidates a bequest.
3
Recognize the concession as removal of delivery impediment
If the heirs voluntarily surrender (سلموا) the two remaining garments to the legatees, the bequest becomes valid in terms of delivery. The impediment is not of validity but of delivery — the heirs' denial of rights.
The text distinguishes between māni' al-ṣiḥḥa (impediment of validity) and māni' al-taslīm (impediment of delivery). The jahāla remains, but consent removes the denial.
4
Apply the division formula
The division is: The legatee of the good garment takes two-thirds of the better of the two remaining; the legatee of the inferior takes two-thirds of the inferior; the legatee of the medium takes one-third of each remaining garment.
This specific distribution resolves the uncertainty proportionally.
5
Understand the reasoning (taluq of rights)
The medium legatee's right could attach to either remaining garment depending on which was lost; hence he takes a share from both. The good legatee has no claim on the inferior, and vice versa, so they take larger shares of their respective qualities.
The reasoning ensures each legatee receives a fair portion based on their original entitlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبثلاثة أثواب متفاوتة لكل لرجل إن ضاع ثوب ولم يدر أي هو، والورثة تقول : لكل توى حقك بطلت، لكن إن سلموا ما بقي أخذ ذو الجيد ثلثي الأعز، وذو الردئ ثلثي الأخس، وذو المتوسط ثلث كل. أي أوصى بثلاثة أثواب متفاوتة : جيد، ومتوسط، ورديء، وقال : الجيد لزيد، والمتوسط لعمرو، والرديء لبكر، فهلك واحد ولا يدرى أي هو، والورثة تقول : لكل واحد هلك حقك، فالوصية باطلة، لكن الورثة إن تسامحوا وسلموا الثوبين الباقيين إلى زيد وعمرو وبكر، أخذ زيد ثلثي الأجود من الثوبين، وأخذ بكر ثلثي الرديء، وعمر ثلث كل واحد. الوصية للقاتل، وهذا بخلاف ما إذا أقر بعين أو دين لوارثه، وللأجنبي حيث لا يصح في حق الأجنبي أيضاً، كما لا يصح في حق الوارث. كذا في الشروح. قوله : بطلت؛ لجهالة المستحق : أي الموصى له كوصية لأحد هذين الرجلين. قوله : لكن إن سلموا ما بقي؛ من الأثواب الثلاثة فتعود صحيحة لزوال المانع من التسليم، لا المانع من الصحة؛ لأن المانع منهما الجهالة، وهي باقية، والمانع من التسليم هو الجحود؛ أي جحود الورثة بقاء حق كل، فتقسم بأن يأخذ ذو الجيد؛ أي الجيد في نفس الأمر ثلثي الأعز إلى الجيد... الخ. ووجه هذه القسمة : أن ذا الوسط حقه في الجيد من الباقيين إن كان الهالك أرفع منهما، وإن كان أردأ منهما فحقه في الرديء منهما، فتعلق حقه مرة بهذا ومرة بالآخر، وإن كان الهالك هو الوسط فلا حق له فيهما. فقد تعلق حقه بكل واحد من الباقين في حال ولم يتعلق في الحالين، فيأخذ ثلث كل منهما، وذو الجيد مدعي الجيد منهما لا الرديء، إذ لا حق له فيه قطعاً، وذو الرديء يدعي الرديء لا الجيد، فيسلم ثلثا الجيد لذي الجيد، وثلثا الرديء لذي الرديء. هكذا ذكر صاحب رد المحتار ناقلاً عن «شرح الجامع الخاني».
And with three garments of different [quality] for each man: if a garment is lost and it is not known which one, and the heirs say: 'For each, your right has perished, so it is invalid.' Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a bequest of three garments of different quality when one is lost and it is unknown which. The passage begins with the main ruling: if the heirs concede, a specific proportional division applies. The commentary then explains the scenario: an individual bequeaths a good garment to Zayd, a medium one to Amr, and an inferior one to Bakr. However, if the heirs voluntarily surrender the two remaining garments, the division is: Zayd (good) takes two-thirds of the better of the two, Amr (medium) takes one-third of each, and Bakr (inferior) takes two-thirds of the inferior. The passage also briefly notes the rule for bequest to a killer and distinguishes it from acknowledgment to an heir or stranger, but does not develop that point. The author cites Radd al-Muhtar for this division, indicating it is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms

جهالة (jahāla): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding the legatee or the subject matter of the bequest.
مانع (māni'): An impediment that prevents the validity or execution of the bequest.

Bequest of a Specific Room in a Shared House
Ruling on bequest of a specific room in a jointly owned house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on what a legatee receives when a bequeathed specific room in a co-owned house falls to the partner's share after division, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
The legatee's entitlement depends on whether division is seen as separation or exchange.

When someone bequeaths a specific room in a house they co-own, the house must be divided. But what if the room ends up in the partner's share? The Hanafi school has a nuanced answer, with an important disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and the practical difference in outcomes.

Guided Path
1
State the Case
Identify the core scenario: Zayd bequeaths a specific room in a house co-owned with Bakr. The house is divided. Determine what happens to the bequest depending on which share the room falls into.
2
Identify Both Hanafi Positions
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the legatee gets the full cubit-measure of the room from the testator's share if the room falls to the partner. Then state Muhammad's position: the legatee gets only half that measure.
3
Analyze the Reasoning Behind Each View
Understand why Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf treat division as separation (ifraz) rather than exchange (mubadala), and why Muhammad treats it as a full exchange. Note the analogy to bequest of another's property and subsequent purchase.
4
Compare the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Compute the practical difference: under the first view, the legatee receives a larger portion from the testator's estate than under Muhammad's view. Evaluate which view is more consistent with the testator's intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وببيت معين من دار مشتركة، قسمت فإن أصاب الموصي، فهو للموصى له، وإلا فله قدره. أوصى زيد لعمرو ببيت معين من دار مشتركة بين زيد وبكر، يجب أن تقسم الدار، فإن وقع البيت في نصيب زيد، فهو للموصى له، وإن وقع في نصيب الشريك فللموصى له مثل ذراع ذلك البيت من نصيب الموصي، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وعند محمد له مثل ذراع نصف ذلك البيت. قوله : وعند محمد ... الخ؛ لأن الموصي أوصى بما يملكه وبما لا يملكه؛ لأن الدار بجميع أجزائها مشتركة، فنفذ الأول؛ أي الوصية بملكه وتوقف الوصية بملك غيره على إجازة صاحبه، وهو إن ملك بعد ذلك بالقسمة التي هي مبادلة لا تنفذ الوصية السابقة. كما إذا أوصى بملك الغير ثم اشتراه ثم إذا قسموها، ووقع البيت في نصيب الموصي تنفذ الوصية في عين الموصي به، وهو نصف البيت، وإن وقع في نصيب صاحبه له مثل ذرع نصف البيت، تنفيذا للوصية في بدل الموصى به عند فواته؛ كالجارية الموصى بها إذا قتلت خطأ تنفذ الوصية في بدلهما. بخلاف ما إذا بيع العبد الموصى به، حيث لا يتعلق الوصية بثمنه؛ لأن الوصية تبطل بالإقدام على البيع على ما مر في مسائل الرجوع عن الوصية. ولهما : إنه أوصى بما يستقر ملكه فيه بالقسمة؛ لأن الظاهر أنه يقصد الإيصاء بملك منتفع به من كل وجه، وذلك يكون بالقسمة؛ لأن الانتفاع بالمشاع قاصر، وقد استقر ملكه في جميع البيت إذا وقع في نصيبه، فتنفذ الوصية فيه. ومعنى المبادلة في هذه القسمة تابع، وإنما المقصود الإفراز تكميلاً للمنفعة؛ ولهذا يجبر على القسمة فيه. وعلى اعتبار الإفراز يصير كأن البيت ملكه من الابتداء، وإن وقع في نصيب الآخر تنفذ في قدر ذرعان جميعه مما وقع في نصيبه، إما لأنه عوضه كما ذكرناه، أو لأن مراد الموصي من ذكر البيت التقدير به تحصيلاً لمقصوده ما أمكن، إلا أنه يتعين البيت إذا وقع في نصيبه جمعاً بين الجهتين التقدير والتمليك، وإن وقع في نصيب الآخر عملنا
And with a specific room in a shared house: it is divided; if it falls to the testator, it is for the legatee; otherwise he gets its measure. Zayd bequeathed to Amr a specific room in a house shared between Zayd and Bakr. The house must be divided. If the room falls in Zayd's share, it is for the legatee; if it falls in the partner's share, then for the legatee is like the cubit-measure of that room from the testator's share. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And according to Muhammad, for him is like the cubit-measure of half of that room. His statement: 'And according to Muhammad...' because the testator bequeathed what he owns and what he does not own; because the house in all its parts is shared, so the first—i.e., the bequest of his own property—is executed, and the bequest of another's property is suspended on its owner's permission. And if he [the testator] later owns it through division, which is an exchange, the previous bequest does not execute. As if he bequeathed another's property then bought it, then when they divide and the room falls in the testator's share, the bequest executes on the very bequeathed thing, which is half the room; and if it falls in his partner's share, he has like the cubit-measure of half the room, executing the bequest on a substitute for the bequeathed thing when it is lost; like a slave-girl who is bequeathed and then killed by mistake—the bequest executes on her substitute. Unlike if the bequeathed slave is sold, where the bequest does not attach to his price, because the bequest becomes invalid by proceeding with the sale, as previously mentioned in the matters of revocation of bequest. And for them both [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]: He bequeathed what his ownership becomes settled in through division, because apparently he intends to bequeath property that can be benefited from in every respect, and that occurs through division, because benefit from shared property is limited, and his ownership becomes settled in the entire room if it falls in his share, so the bequest executes on it. And the meaning of exchange in this division is subsidiary; rather the purpose is separation to complete the benefit; therefore one is compelled to division in it. And based on the consideration of separation, it becomes as if the room was his property from the beginning. And if it falls in the other's share, it executes to the extent of the cubit-measure of all of it from what falls in his share, either because it is a substitute as we mentioned, or because the testator's intention in mentioning the room is to estimate by it to achieve his intention as much as possible, but the room is determined if it falls in his share, combining the two aspects of estimation and ownership, and if it falls in the other's share we act...
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when someone bequeaths a specific room in a house that is co-owned with another person. The main ruling states that the house must be divided; if the room ends up in the testator's share, the legatee gets the room; otherwise, he gets an equivalent measure from the testator's share. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the legatee gets the full measure of the room from the testator's share, while Muhammad holds that he gets only half that measure. The commentary explains the reasoning: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the testator's ownership becomes complete in the room after division, so the bequest executes fully; if it falls to the partner, the legatee gets a substitute from the testator's share. Muhammad's view is that since the testator initially only owned a share, the bequest is partly for his own property and partly for another's, and when the room falls to the partner, the legatee only gets the value of half the room (the testator's share). The commentary also compares this with cases of bequest of another's property that is later owned, or a bequeathed slave-girl who is killed. The passage concludes with the preferred view that combines estimation and ownership.

Key Terms
بيت معين (bayt mu'ayyan): A specific room or house that is identified and designated in the bequest.
قسمة (qisma): Division of jointly owned property into separate shares, often to enable individual use.
ذراع (dhira'): A cubit measure used to estimate the size or value of the room.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if a bequeathed specific room in a shared house falls to the partner's share after division, what does the legatee receive?
A) Nothing, because the bequest is void.
B) The exact same room from the partner's share.
C) A cubit-measure equal to the entire room from the testator's share.
D) A cubit-measure equal to half the room from the testator's share.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a bequest of a specific room in a co-owned house is valid, and if the room falls to the partner, the legatee receives an equivalent measure from the testator's share, with a disagreement on whether it is the full room or just half.

Bequest from Common Property: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Division
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest from common property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing shares when a bequest is made from jointly owned property and calculate the different shares according to Imam Muhammad versus the two companions.

Core Idea
When a bequest is from common property, the legatee's share depends on whether we value the specific item proportionally (Imam Muhammad) or as a whole (Sahibayn).

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the allocation of a bequest from jointly owned property. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah presents a concrete example: a testator bequeaths a specific house that is part of a shared courtyard. The disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) centers on how to divide the testator's share when the bequeathed item falls into the non-testator's portion. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to handle fractional ownership in wills.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the core disagreement
Identify the facts: a testator bequeaths a house (10 cubits) from a shared courtyard (100 cubits). The house falls into the share of the co-owner. Both parties agree the bequest is valid, but disagree on how to allocate the testator's share.
The testator owns half the courtyard, i.e., 50 cubits.
2
Calculate Imam Muhammad's division
Imam Muhammad treats the house as jointly owned, so the testator only owns half the house (5 cubits). The testator's share is 50 cubits total. The legatee gets 5, the heirs get the remaining 45. Divide the 50 into 10 shares of 5 cubits each: legatee 1, heirs 9.
Ratio: legatee gets 1/10 of testator's share.
3
Calculate the two companions' division
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani treat the house as a specific entity; the legatee is entitled to the whole house (10 cubits). The testator's share is 50 cubits, but now the legatee takes 10, leaving 40 for heirs? Wait, the text says heirs get 45? Let's check: total testator's share is 50. If legatee takes 10, heirs get 40. But the text says heirs get 45 - that indicates the testator's share is actually 55? Let's re-read: the text says 'they get forty-five', perhaps implying the testator's share is 55 (house 10 + courtyard 45). Actually, the courtyard is 100, half is 50. The house is 10, so if the house is entirely in the testator's share, then testator's share includes the house (10) plus 40 from the rest. But the house falls into the non-testator's share, so the testator's share is just the rest of the courtyard excluding the house: 45. Then the testator's share is 45? No, the text says 'his share is divided' - his share is the testator's share. But if the house is not in his share, his share is only the remaining 45. Then the example would be: testator owns half the courtyard (50), but the house is in the other half. So the testator's share is 50, but the house is not in it. So how can he bequeath a house he doesn't own? The passage says 'the house falls into the share of the non-testator' - so the testator does not own it. This is a problem. Actually, the bequest is of a house that is in the courtyard, and the testator is a co-owner. If the house is physically part of the jointly owned property, the testator owns a share of it. The scenario: courtyard 100 cubits, house 10 cubits. The testator owns half the courtyard by value? Actually, the text says 'the courtyard is 100 cubits, the house is 10 cubits' - likely the house is a building within the courtyard, and the total property is 100 cubits including the house? The interpretation: the courtyard is 100 cubits, and the house occupies 10 cubits thereof. So the total property is 100 cubits. The testator owns half of the entire property, i.e., 50 cubits. The house is 10 cubits, so it represents 10% of the property. If the house falls into the non-testator's share (i.e., after division, the house goes to the co-owner), then the testator's share is the remaining 40 cubits plus half the house? No, the text says 'the house falls into the share of the non-testator' - meaning when the property is partitioned, the house goes entirely to the co-owner. So the testator's share is the rest of the property: 100 - 10 = 90 cubits, but he only owns half? This is confusing. Let's trust the text: it says 'his share is divided between the legatee and the heirs into ten shares: nine for the heirs and one for the legatee. And this according to Muhammad: the legatee gets five cubits (half the house) and the heirs get half the courtyard excluding the house, which is forty-five, so every five cubits is a share, resulting in ten.' This implies the testator's share is 50 cubits (45 + 5). So the testator owns half of the courtyard excluding the house (45) plus half of the house (5) = 50. That makes sense: the testator owns 50% of the entire 100 cubits, so he owns 5 cubits of the house and 45 cubits of the rest. So his total share is 50. Under Imam Muhammad, the legatee gets his share of the house = 5, leaving 45 for heirs. That's 1:9 ratio. Under the two companions, the legatee gets the entire house (10 cubits) from the testator's share, so the testator's share is 50, but the legatee takes 10, leaving 40 for heirs. But the text says 'the shares become eleven: for the legatee two shares, for them nine.' That ratio is 2:9, so the testator's share would be 11 shares of 5 cubits each = 55 cubits. Wait, that adds up to 55? The testator's share cannot be 55 if he only owns half of 100. There's a mismatch. Actually, the text says 'heirs get forty-five' and then 'it is divided into eleven shares because the legatee gets ten and they get forty-five, so the shares become eleven: for the legatee two shares, for them nine.' The total is 10+45=55 cubits. That would be the testator's share? But we said testator's share is 50. Let's re-read: The passage says 'the courtyard is one hundred cubits, and the house is ten cubits, his share is divided between the legatee and the heirs on ten shares: nine for the heirs and one for the legatee. This according to Muhammad: the legatee gets five cubits half the house, and the heirs get half the courtyard excluding the house, which is forty-five, so every five cubits is a share, resulting in ten. And according to both: it is divided into eleven shares, because the legatee gets ten and they get forty-five, so the shares become eleven: for the legatee two shares, for them nine.' So in the second calculation, the total is 55. This implies that the testator's share is not 50 but something else. Perhaps the testator's share includes the house? Actually, if the testator owns half the property, his share is 50. But the house is 10. If the house is in the testator's share, then his share includes the house plus 40. But the text says 'the house falls into the share of the non-testator', so the testator does not have the house in his share. So his share consists only of the rest of the courtyard, which is 90 (since the house is 10 of 100), and he owns half of that 90? That would be 45. So the testator's share is 45. Then Imam Muhammad: legatee gets half the house (5) from somewhere? But the house is not in testator's share. This is confusing. Perhaps the scenario is that the testator bequeaths a house that is physically part of the jointly owned property, but the house itself is owned in common. So the testator owns a share of the house as well. When they partition, the house might go to one party or the other. In the example, after partition, the house falls in the non-testator's portion, meaning the testator loses his share of the house. But the testator's share is still half of the total property value. So if the house is 10, and it goes to the other, the testator must get an equivalent value from elsewhere. That might be why the numbers work out differently. To avoid confusion, I will stick to the numbers given in the text: according to Imam Muhammad: 1 out of 10 shares for legatee; according to both: 2 out of 11 shares for legatee. The guided_path should just present these numbers as given.
The key is the ratio: 1/10 vs 2/11.
4
Identify the underlying legal principle difference
Imam Muhammad views the bequest as a share of the common property, so the legatee gets only the testator's proportional share of the specific item. The two companions view the bequest as an entitlement to the specific item itself, so the legatee gets the full item from the testator's overall share.
This reflects a broader difference in how to value a bequest of an 'ayn from mushtarak.
5
Contrast with the ruling for acknowledgment (iqrar)
The passage compares wasiyyah to iqrar. In iqrar, if someone acknowledges a house from shared property, the ruling is similar but with some differences: consensus that Muhammad agrees with the two companions on iqrar, unlike in wasiyyah. The distinction is that iqrar of another's property is valid even if the acknowledger does not own it, whereas wasiyyah of another's property is invalid.
This highlights the specificity of the wasiyyah rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما في الإقرار، وبألف عُيِّن من مال غير له الإجازة بعد موت الموصي ، والمنع بعدها كما في الإقرار أي إن كان مكان الوصية إقرار، فالحكم كذلك، قيل: بالإجماع ، وقيل : فيه خلاف محمد الله. (٢) ( وبألف عين من مال غير له الإجازة بعد موت الموصي، والمنع بعدها): بالتقدير، أو لأنه أراد التقدير على اعتبار أخذ الوجهين والتمليك بعينه على اعتبار الوجه الآخر. ثم إذا وقع البيتُ في نصيب غير الموصي والدارُ مئة ذراع، والبيت عشرة أذرع ، يقسم نصيبه بين الموصى له وبين الورثة على عشرة أسهم ، تسعة منها للورثة وسهم للموصى له. وهذا عند محمد ه، فيضرب الموصى بخمسة أذرع نصف البيت والورثة بنصف الدار سوى البيت، وهو خمسة وأربعون ، فيجعل كلّ خمسة سهما، فيصير عشرة. وعندهما يقسم على أحد عشر سهماً ؛ لأنَّ الموصى له يضرب بالعشرة، وهم بخمسة وأربعين، فتصير السهام أحد عشر للموصى له سهمان، ولهم تسعة. كذا في «الهداية». قوله : إن كان مكان الوصية ... الخ ؛ أي إقرار البيت من دار مشتركة مثل الوصية به، حتى يؤمر بتسليم كله إن وقع البيتُ في نصيب المقرّ عندهما ، وإن وقع في نصيب الآخر يؤمر بتسليم مثله ، وعند محمد الله يؤمر بتسليم النصف أو قدر النصف. كذا في «الزيلعي». قوله : قيل بالإجماع ؛ أي قيل : محمد الله في الإقرار معهما لا خلاف فيه ، فالفرق له : أنَّ الإقرار بملك الغير صحيح، حتى أنَّ من أقر بملك الغير لغيره ثم ملكه يؤمر بالتسليم إلى المقرّ له ، والوصية بملك الغير لا تصح، حتى لو ملكـه بـوجـه مـن الوجوه، ثم مات لا تصح وصيّته ولا تنفذ. كذا في «الهداية». قوله : والمنع بعدها ؛ أي له أن يمنع من التسليم بعد الإجازة ؛ لأنَّ هذا تبرع
As in acknowledgment, and with a specified thousand from the property of another, he has permission after the death of the testator, and the prohibition after it, as in acknowledgment, i.e., if the place of bequest is acknowledgment, the ruling is the same. It was said: by consensus, and it was said: there is a difference of opinion with Muhammad. (2) (And with a specified thousand from property of another, he has permission after the death of the testator, and the prohibition after it): by estimation, or because he intended estimation considering taking two aspects, and ownership of the specific thing considering the other aspect. Then if the house falls into the share of the non-testator and the courtyard is one hundred cubits, and the house is ten cubits, his share is divided between the legatee and the heirs into ten shares: nine for the heirs and one for the legatee. And this according to Muhammad: the legatee gets five cubits (half the house) and the heirs get half the courtyard excluding the house, which is forty-five, so every five cubits is made a share, resulting in ten. According to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): it is divided into eleven shares, because the legatee gets ten (cubits) and they get forty-five, so the shares become eleven: for the legatee two shares, for them nine. Thus in Al-Hidayah. He said: If the place of bequest is ... etc., i.e., acknowledgment of a house from a shared courtyard is like the bequest of it, so that he is ordered to deliver all of it if the house falls into the share of the acknowledging party according to them, and if it falls into the share of the other, he is ordered to deliver its equivalent, and according to Muhammad he is ordered to deliver half or the equivalent of half. Thus in Al-Zayla'i. He said: It was said by consensus; i.e., it was said: there is no disagreement of Muhammad with them regarding acknowledgment, so the difference for him is that acknowledgment of ownership of another is valid, such that if someone acknowledges ownership of another to someone else and then becomes owner of it, he is ordered to deliver it to the acknowledgee, while bequest of property belonging to another is not valid, such that even if he acquires it in some way and then dies, his bequest is not valid and is not executed. Thus in Al-Hidayah. He said: And the prohibition after it; i.e., he may prevent delivery after permission, because this is a gratuitous act.
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the division of shares when a bequest is made from jointly owned property. The text first presents a general rule: if a bequest is made out of property belonging to another (i.e., the testator bequeaths a specific item that is not entirely his), the bequest is suspended pending the heirs' permission after death; otherwise it is void. Then it gives a concrete example: a courtyard of 100 cubits containing a house of 10 cubits. The testator bequeaths the house but the house falls into the share of the non-testator (i.e., the other co-owner). The division of the testator's share (which is half the courtyard?) is then calculated. According to Imam Muhammad, the legatee is entitled to half the house (5 cubits) and the heirs get the remaining half of the courtyard excluding the house (45 cubits); thus the testator's share is divided into 10 parts, with the legatee getting 1 part. According to both Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions), the legatee gets the full 10 cubits of the house, and the heirs get 45 cubits, making a total of 55 cubits, so the testator's share is divided into 11 parts, with the legatee getting 2 parts. The commentary clarifies that this difference arises from how the testator's share is valued: Imam Muhammad considers the house as owned in common (so the legatee gets only half), while the two companions consider the house as a specific entity whose value is its whole. The passage then compares this to an acknowledgment (iqrar) of a house from a shared property: if someone acknowledges another's ownership of a specified house in a shared courtyard, the ruling is similar but with variations among the imams. Finally, it distinguishes between bequest and acknowledgment: acknowledgment of another's property is valid even if the acknowledgee does not own it, whereas bequest of another's property is invalid unless the testator later acquires it.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will: a disposition of property to take effect after death.
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Acknowledgment: admitting that property belongs to another.
المشترك (al-mushtarak): Jointly owned property; common property.
تقدير (taqdir): Estimation; valuation of a share rather than a specific item.
تمليك بعينه (tamlik bi-'aynih): Transfer of ownership of a specific item itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example from the passage, how many shares does the legatee receive according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani)?
A) 1 share out of 10
B) 2 shares out of 11
C) 5 shares out of 55
D) 1 share out of 11

Key Takeaway
When a bequest is made from jointly owned property, the legatee's entitlement depends on whether you value the bequest proportionally (Imam Muhammad) or as a specific item (the two companions), resulting in a different share division.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
