Definitions of In-Laws and Family in a Will
Defines terms for in-laws and family in will context

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of sihr, khatan, and ahl in the context of a will and apply them to determine beneficiaries.

Core Idea
In a will, 'in-laws' and 'sons-in-law' refer to specific prohibited relatives, not the entire extended family.

When a testator uses terms like 'my in-laws' or 'my family' in a will, the Hanafi school has precise definitions that determine who inherits. This lesson clarifies the meanings of sihr, khatan, and ahl as defined by Imam Muhammad, based on prophetic practice and linguistic analysis. Understanding these definitions is crucial for correctly executing a bequest and avoiding disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its context
The terms sihr (in-laws), khatan (son-in-law), and ahl (family) are used in wills. The passage defines each according to Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.
Context matters: these definitions are specific to bequests.
2
Understand the definition of sihr
Sihr refers to every blood relative of the testator's wife who is prohibited for marriage (muharram), such as her father, brother, uncle. This is based on the Prophet's practice when he married Juwayriyya.
Imam Muhammad's broader interpretation is the relied-upon view.
3
Understand the definition of khatan
Khatan refers to every husband of a female relative who is prohibited for marriage to the testator, such as son-in-law (daughter's husband), brother-in-law (sister's husband), etc.
The term also includes prohibited male relatives of the husband.
4
Understand the definition of ahl
When a will says 'for the family of so-and-so', ahl is interpreted as the wife (zawja) according to Abu Hanifa.
This is a restricted meaning for will contexts.
5
Apply the definitions
If a testator bequeaths to his 'as-har', the beneficiaries are all his wife's muharram relatives. If to 'akhtan', beneficiaries are husbands of his muharram female relatives. If to 'ahl' of a person, it means his wife.
All recipients share equally in the one-third, regardless of proximity or freedom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصهره : كلُّ ذي رحم محرم من عرسه . وختنه : كُل زوج ذات رحم محرم منه". وأهله : عرسه). هذا عند أبي حنيفة له
قوله : وصهره ؛ - بكسر الصاد المهملة - : كل ذي رحم محرم من زوجته كآبائها وأعمامها وأخوالها وأخواتها وغيرهم ، لما روي أنه لما تزوج جويرية له أعتق كل ملك من ذي رحم محرم منها ، وكانوا يسمون أصهار النبي ، فمن أوصى لأصهاره، فالوصية لكلِّ ذي رحم محرَّم من امرأته، وهذا التفسير اختار محمد . وقال في «الصحاح : الأصهار أهلُ بيت المرأة، وقال في «مجمل اللغة»: قال الخليل : لا يقال لأهل بيت المرأة إلا الأصهار ، وقال فخر الإسلام في «شرح الروايات»: أمّا الصهرُ فقد يطلق على الختن، لكن الغالب ما ذكره محمد ه. كذا في «غاية البيان.
وفي «الهداية»(۲): وكذا يدخل فيه كل ذي رحم محرم من زوجة أبيه، وزوجة ابنه وزوجة كلّ ذي رحم محرم منه ؛ لأن الكل أصهار. انتهى. [٢] قوله : زوج كلّ ذاتِ رحم محرم منه ؛ كأزواج البنات والأخوات والعمات والخالات وغيرهن، وهذا المشهور.
قال في «العناية» (۳) : الختان كما يطلق على أزواج المحارم يطلق على محارم الأزواج، فمن أوصى لأختانه فالوصيّة لزوج كلّ ذاتِ رحم محرم منه، ويكون كل ذي رحم من أزواج المحارم من الذكر والأنثى، ومحارم الأزواج كلهم في قسمة الثلث سواء. وفي «الهداية» : ويستوي فيه الحر والعبد، والأقرب والأبعد ؛ لأنّ اللفظ يتناول الكل.
[٣]قوله : وأهله عرسه ؛ فمَن أوصى لأهل فلان فهي على زوجته عند الأعظم
And his in-laws (sihr): every relative through marriage who is prohibited (muharram) from his wife. And his son-in-law (khatan): every husband of a female relative who is prohibited from him. And his family (ahl): his wife. This is according to Abu Hanifa.
He said: 'And his in-laws (sihr)' — with a kasra on the sad — every relative through marriage prohibited from his wife, like her fathers, uncles, maternal uncles, sisters, and others. Because it is narrated that when he married Juwayriyya, he freed every slave who was a prohibited relative of hers, and they were called the in-laws (as-har) of the Prophet. So whoever makes a will for his in-laws, the bequest is for every prohibited relative of his wife. This interpretation is chosen by Muhammad (al-Shaybani). In al-Sihah it is said: The in-laws are the wife's family. In Mujmal al-Lugha it is said: al-Khalil said: The wife's family are only called in-laws. And Fakhr al-Islam said in Sharh al-Riwayat: The term sihr may be applied to son-in-law, but the predominant is what Muhammad mentioned. This is in Ghayat al-Bayan.
In al-Hidayah: And also included in it is every prohibited relative of the wife of his father, and the wife of his son, and of every prohibited relative of his, because all are in-laws. End.
He said: 'husband of every female prohibited relative' such as the husbands of daughters, sisters, paternal aunts, maternal aunts, and others. This is the well-known position.
He said in al-Inaya: The term khatan is applied both to the husbands of prohibited female relatives and to the prohibited male relatives of the husband. So whoever makes a will for his sons-in-law (akhtan), the bequest is for every husband of a prohibited female relative, and every male or female relative from the husbands of prohibited women and the prohibited men of husbands are all equal in the division of the third. In al-Hidayah: The free and slave, the near and far are equal; because the term encompasses all.
He said: 'And his family, his wife'; so whoever makes a will for the family of so-and-so, it refers to his wife according to the greatest (al-a'zam).
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage is a definitional ruling that clarifies the terms 'sihr' (in-laws), 'khatan' (son-in-law), and 'ahl' (family) when used in a will. According to Abu Hanifa, 'sihr' refers to all blood relatives of the testator's wife who are prohibited for marriage (muharram), such as her parents, siblings, uncles, etc. This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who freed such relatives when he married Juwayriyya and they were called his 'as-har'. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani chose this interpretation. The term 'khatan' (plural akhtan) refers to the husbands of female relatives who are prohibited for marriage to the testator, such as the husbands of daughters, sisters, aunts. Both groups are included in the bequest, and the recipients share equally in the one-third of the estate. The term 'ahl' (family) when used in a will (e.g., 'for the family of so-and-so') is interpreted as the wife (zawja) according to the predominant view (al-a'zam, i.e., Abu Hanifa). The passage notes equality among recipients regardless of freedom, slavery, proximity, or distance.

Key Terms
صهر (ṣihr): A relative through marriage (in-law), specifically a prohibited relative (muharram) of the testator's wife.
ختن (khatan): Son-in-law: the husband of a female relative who is prohibited for marriage to the testator.
أهل (ahl): Family, but in the context of a will for 'ahl' of someone, it refers to the wife (zawja) according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the implication for a bequest made to 'as-hari' (my in-laws)?
A) It goes to the testator's wife only.
B) It goes to every blood relative of the testator who is prohibited for marriage.
C) It goes to every prohibited relative (muharram) of the testator's wife.
D) It goes to the testator's children and grandchildren.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, bequest terms like sihr, khatan, and ahl have specific legal meanings that determine the beneficiaries, and the relied-upon interpretation follows Imam Muhammad's broader definitions.

Definitions of Sihr, Khitan, and Ahl in Wasiyyah
Defining key terms for wasiyyah beneficiaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sihr (as-har), khatan (akhtan), and ahl in the context of bequests and apply these definitions to determine the beneficiaries of a wasiyyah.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, as-har means the wife's mahram relatives, akhtan are husbands of one's mahram females, and ahl means the wife.

In the book of wasiyyah, precise definitions determine who receives a bequest. The terms as-har, akhtan, and ahl often appear in wills, and the Hanafi school has specific interpretations. This lesson unpacks these definitions from the commentary on al-Wiqayah, drawing on the authority of Imam Muhammad and al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three terms and their general meanings
Note the terms 'as-har' (plural of sihr), 'akhtan' (plural of khatan), and 'ahl'. Understand that they refer to different categories of relatives by marriage.
These terms are often misunderstood in everyday language.
2
Analyze the definition of sihr (as-har)
Examine the text: 'every blood relative unlawful to marry from his wife'. This includes the wife's father, brother, uncle, etc. The commentator endorses Imam Muhammad's interpretation and notes that al-Hidayah extends it to relatives through other marital links.
The Prophet's treatment of Juwayriyah's relatives serves as evidence.
3
Analyze the definition of khatan (akhtan)
Read: 'every husband of a female blood relative unlawful to marry from him'. This covers sons-in-law, brothers-in-law, etc. The bequest is shared equally among all such husbands, regardless of status.
Al-Hidayah states free and slave, near and far are equal.
4
Understand the definition of ahl and its application
The text clarifies that 'ahl' in this context means the wife. So a bequest 'to the ahl of so-and-so' goes to his wife.
This is a specific legal meaning; in other contexts ahl may include family.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وصهره: كل ذي رحم محرم من عرسه، وختنه: كل زوج ذات رحم محرم منه، وأهله: عرسه. هذا عند أبي حنيفة له.
[1] قوله: وصهره: كل ذي رحم محرم من زوجته كآبائها وأعمامها وأخوالها وأخواتها وغيرهم، لما روي أنه لما تزوج جويرية أعتق كل ملك من ذي رحم محرم منها، وكانوا يسمون أصهار النبي، فمن أوصى لأصهاره، فالوصية لكل ذي رحم محرم من امرأته، وهذا التفسير اختار محمد. وقال في الصحاح: الأصهار أهل بيت المرأة، وقال في مجمل اللغة: قال الخليل: لا يقال لأهل بيت المرأة إلا الأصهار، وقال فخر الإسلام في شرح الروايات: أما الصهر فقد يطلق على الختن، لكن الغالب ما ذكره محمد. كذا في غاية البيان.
وفي الهداية: وكذا يدخل فيه كل ذي رحم محرم من زوجة أبيه، وزوجة ابنه وزوجة كل ذي رحم محرم منه؛ لأن الكل أصهار. انتهى.

[3] قوله: وأهله عرسه؛ فمن أوصى لأهل فلان فهي على زوجته عند الأعظم
Book of Bequests / Its Definition and Rulings. And his as-har: every blood relative unlawful to marry from his wife, and his akhtan: every husband of a female blood relative unlawful to marry from him, and his ahl: his wife. This is according to Abu Hanifa. [1] His saying: 'and his as-har': every blood relative unlawful to marry from his wife, like her fathers, paternal uncles, maternal uncles, sisters, and others, because it is narrated that when he married Juwayriyah, he freed every slave who was a blood relative unlawful to marry from her, and they were called the as-har of the Prophet. So whoever makes a bequest to his as-har, the bequest is for every blood relative unlawful to marry from his wife, and this interpretation was chosen by Muhammad. It is said in al-Sihah: al-as-har are the family of the woman. It is said in Mujmal al-Lugha: al-Khalil said: the family of the woman are only called al-as-har. Fakhr al-Islam said in Sharh al-Riwayat: as for sihr, it may be applied to the son-in-law, but the predominant is what Muhammad mentioned. So in Ghayat al-Bayan. And in al-Hidayah: likewise enters into it every blood relative unlawful to marry from the wife of his father, and the wife of his son, and the wife of every blood relative unlawful to marry from him, because all are as-har. End. [2] His saying: 'husband of every female blood relative unlawful to marry from him': like the husbands of daughters, sisters, paternal aunts, maternal aunts, and others, and this is the well-known. He said in al-Inayah: al-akhtan, just as it is applied to the husbands of female relatives, is applied to the female relatives of husbands. So whoever makes a bequest to his akhtan, the bequest is for the husband of every female blood relative unlawful to marry from him, and every blood relative from the husbands of female relatives, male and female, and all the female relatives of husbands are equal in the division of the third. And in al-Hidayah: the free and the slave, the near and the far are equal in it, because the word encompasses all. [3] His saying: 'and his ahl: his wife'; so whoever makes a bequest to the ahl of so-and-so, it refers to his wife according to the greatest [imam].
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah defines three terms related to bequests: as-har (in-laws), akhtan (sons-in-law/brothers-in-law), and ahl (family). The commentator explains each term and the ruling for a bequest made to these categories. For as-har, the commentator endorses Imam Muhammad's definition: all blood relatives from the wife's side who are mahram (unlawful to marry). This is supported by the incident of the Prophet marrying Juwayriyah and freeing her relatives. The definition is broadened in al-Hidayah to include relatives through the father's wife, son's wife, etc. For akhtan, the well-known definition is husbands of female blood relatives (e.g., daughters, sisters). A bequest to akhtan goes to these husbands, and all such husbands share equally in the one-third of the estate, regardless of being free or slave, near or distant relative. Finally, ahl is interpreted as the wife; a bequest to the ahl of someone refers to that person's wife. The passage follows the author's order of defining each term and then stating the ruling.

Key Terms
صهر (sihr): Every blood relative from the wife's side who is mahram (unlawful to marry), such as her father, uncle, brother, etc.
ختن (khatan): The husband of a female blood relative who is mahram (unlawful to marry), e.g., son-in-law, brother-in-law.
أهل (ahl): Specifically the wife; a bequest to the ahl of a person goes to his wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wasiyyah, precise definitions apply: as-har are wife's mahram relatives, akhtan are husbands of mahram females, and ahl means the wife.

Distribution of Bequest Among Paternal and Maternal Uncles
Explaining distribution of bequest among paternal and maternal uncles with an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa prioritizes closeness (aqrabiyya) in distributing a bequest among paternal and maternal uncles, and distinguish his position from the Sahibayn's equal distribution.

Core Idea
In a bequest to relatives, paternal uncles take priority over maternal uncles because lineage is through the father.

This passage explores an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the distribution of a bequest when the testator has paternal and maternal uncles. The core principle is 'al-aqrab fa al-aqrab' (the closest, then the closest). Abu Hanifa uses this principle and an analogy from marriage guardianship to give paternal uncles a larger share, while the Sahibayn disregard closeness and divide equally. Understanding this dispute illuminates how legal reasoning (qiyas) and customary principles shape Hanafi inheritance law.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the positions
Identify the factual scenarios: (A) two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles; (B) one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles. For each, state the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
Abu Hanifa gives all or half to paternal uncles; Sahibayn divide equally among individuals.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Understand why Abu Hanifa considers paternal uncles closer: they are from the father's side, and a person is attributed to his father. Also, analogy from marriage guardianship (wilaya fil-nikah) where paternal uncle has priority over maternal uncle.
This is a qiyas based on established legal closeness.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's reasoning
The Sahibayn do not consider closeness (aqrabiyya) in this context; they distribute equally among all uncles, treating each as an individual relative equally entitled.
They presumably interpret the will literally without inferring preference for lineage.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Calculate the practical difference in shares: In scenario (A), Abu Hanifa gives all to the two paternal uncles; Sahibayn give each of the four uncles 1/4. In scenario (B), Abu Hanifa gives 1/2 to the paternal uncle and 1/2 to the two maternal uncles (i.e., 1/4 each); Sahibayn give each 1/3.
The difference is significant and affects the testator's intended distribution.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and mufta bihi
The commentary supports Abu Hanifa's view, indicating it is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position. Note that this is the position for fatwa.
The tarjih authority is the author of 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, citing the analogy from marriage guardianship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن كان له عمان وخالان فذا لعميه، وفي عم وخالين نصف بينه وبينهما (فإن كان له عمان وخالان ، فذا لعميه ) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له ، وقالا : يقسم بينهم أرباعاً لعدم اعتبار الأقربية. (وفي عم وخالين" نصف بينه وبينهما ؛ لأن أقل الجمع إذا كان اثنين ، ) فللواحدِ النّصفُ بقي النصفُ الآخر، فيكون للخاليين"، وعندهما : يقسم أثلاثا بينهم. من الجانبين، فلا يسمى قريباً. كذا في «غاية البيان». ١ ] قوله : فإن كان له عمّان.... الخ ؛ هذا تفريع على قوله : الأقرب فالأقرب ؛ أي إن كان للموصي عمّان وخالان فذا : أي الموصى به لعميه ؛ لأنهما أقرب من الخالين ؛ لأن قرابتهما من جهة الأب، والإنسان ينسب إلى أبيه. ألا ترى أن الولاية للعم دون الخال في النكاح، فثبت أنهما أقرب من طريق الحكم، «اتقاني»، وهذا حيث كان الوارث غيرهما ، وكذا يقال فيما بعد، وهو ظاهر. هكذا الرد المحتار). (٢) قوله : وفي عم وخالين ... الخ ؛ أي إذا أوصى لأقاربه، وترك عماً وخالين فللعم النصف، والنصف الباقي للخالين ؛ لأنَّ أقلّ الجمع ... الخ، وقوله: نصف صيغة ماضي، مبني على المفعول من التنصيف والضمير يرجع إلى الموصى له. [٣] قوله : فيكون للخالين ؛ لأنَّ اللفظ جمع، فلا بد من اعتبار الجمع فيه وهو الاثنان في الوصية كما مرّ مراراً، فيضم إلى العم الخالان ؛ ليصير جمعاً ، فيأخذ العم النصف ؛ لأنه أقرب، ويأخذ الخالان النصف الباقي ؛ لعدم مـن تقـدم عـلـيـه. كذا في الزَّيْلَعِي. بخلاف ما إذا أوصى لذي قرابة، وللموصي عمّ وخالان، حيث يكون الكل للعم ؛ لأنَّ اللفظ للمفرد، فيحرز الواحد الكلّ ، إذ هو الأقرب. كذا في «الهداية (۳).
If he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest is for his two paternal uncles. And for one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, half is between him (the paternal uncle) and them (the maternal uncles). (If he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then it is for his two paternal uncles) - this is according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf & Muhammad) said: It is divided among them in fourths, due to not considering closeness. (And for one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, half is between him and them, because the least of the plural is two) - so for the one (paternal uncle) is half, and the other half remains, so it is for the two maternal uncles. And according to them, it is divided into thirds among them. From both sides, he is not called a relative. Similarly in Ghayat al-Bayan. 1] His words: "If he has two paternal uncles..." etc.; this is a branch from his saying: "the closest, then the closest"; meaning if the testator has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest is for his two paternal uncles because they are closer than the maternal uncles; because their kinship is from the father's side, and a person is attributed to his father. Do you not see that guardianship in marriage is for the paternal uncle, not the maternal uncle, so it is established that they (paternal uncles) are closer by way of legal ruling. This is as transmitted, and this is when there is no other heir, and likewise it is said later, and it is apparent. Thus from Radd al-Muhtar. (2) His words: "And for one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles..." etc.; meaning if he bequeaths to his relatives and leaves one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle is half, and the remaining half is for the two maternal uncles because the least plural... etc. And his word "nisf" (half) is a past tense verb in the passive voice from "tansif" (to halve), and the pronoun refers to the legatee. [3] His words: "so it is for the two maternal uncles" because the expression is plural, so consideration of the plural is necessary, which is two in a will as mentioned repeatedly, so the maternal uncles are added to the paternal uncle to become a plural, then the paternal uncle takes half because he is closer, and the two maternal uncles take the remaining half because there is no one before them. Thus from al-Zayla'i. Contrary to if he bequeaths to one who has kinship, and the testator has one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then all goes to the paternal uncle because the expression is singular, so the one takes all, as he is the closer. Thus from al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 620

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning how to distribute a bequest among paternal and maternal uncles when the testator has left a will to his relatives. The discussion arises from the principle 'the closest, then the closest' (al-aqrab fa al-aqrab). The author first presents the scenario of two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles. According to Abu Hanifa, the two paternal uncles receive the entire bequest because they are closer in kinship than the maternal uncles. The two companions (Sahibayn, i.e., Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree and hold that the bequest should be divided into four equal shares, one for each uncle, because they do not consider the factor of closeness (aqrabiyya). In the second scenario, if there is one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, Abu Hanifa rules that the paternal uncle takes half the bequest and the two maternal uncles share the other half. This is because the least plural is two, so the paternal uncle is considered one part and the maternal uncles as a pair form the other part. The Sahibayn, however, divide the bequest into three equal shares. The commentary then explains the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's view: paternal uncles are from the father's side, and a person is attributed to the father; moreover, for marriage guardianship, the paternal uncle has priority over the maternal uncle, so paternal uncles are deemed closer by analogy. The text also notes that if the testator had bequeathed to 'a relative' (singular), then with one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, the paternal uncle would take all because the expression is singular. This passage is a clear example of how the Hanafi school uses the principle of closeness (al-aqrabiyya) to resolve conflicts in legacies.

Key Terms
عم ('amm): Paternal uncle (father's brother). In this passage, he is considered a closer relative than the maternal uncle.
خال (khal): Maternal uncle (mother's brother). Considered less close than the paternal uncle.
أقرب (aqrab): Closer in kinship. The basis for distributing the bequest among relatives; the closer relative gets priority.
جمع (jam'): Plural. In the context of a will, the least plural is two, so when the testator uses a plural word, it applies to at least two individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All goes to the paternal uncle.
B) Divided into three equal shares.
C) The paternal uncle gets half, and the two maternal uncles share the other half.
D) The paternal uncle gets one third, and each maternal uncle gets one third.

Key Takeaway
In a bequest to relatives, paternal uncles take priority over maternal uncles because of their closer kinship, as established by the principle of al-aqrab fa al-aqrab and analogy from marriage guardianship.

Bequest Distribution: Paternal vs Maternal Uncles
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest priority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on bequest distribution between paternal and maternal uncles and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with evidence.

Core Idea
Paternal uncles take priority over maternal uncles in bequests due to lineage and analogy to guardianship.

In this passage, we encounter an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the distribution of a bequest (wasiyyah) to relatives. The question arises when the testator leaves a bequest to his relatives and has both paternal and maternal uncles. Abu Hanifa rules that the bequest goes exclusively to the paternal uncles, while the Sahibayn argue for equal division. The commentary provides the reasoning and evidence for Abu Hanifa's position, rooted in the principle of closeness (aqrabiyya) and analogy to guardianship in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
Recognize that the testator has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles. Abu Hanifa says all bequest to paternal uncles; Sahibayn say divide into fourths.
The dispute is about apportionment, not validity of wasiyyah.
2
Trace Abu Hanifa's evidence
Abu Hanifa relies on the principle 'al-aqrab fa al-aqrab' (the nearest, then the nearest). Paternal uncles are closer because they are related through the father. This is supported by analogy (qiyas) to marriage guardianship (wilayah), where paternal uncle takes precedence over maternal uncle.
The qiyas is based on the illah of being from the father's side.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's objection
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that closeness (aqrabiyya) is not a consideration in bequests; all relatives should share equally. Hence they propose dividing the bequest into four equal parts.
Their dalil is absence of textual evidence for aqrabiyya in wasiyyah.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, maternal uncles get nothing; under Sahibayn, each maternal uncle gets one fourth. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is Abu Hanifa's view, as affirmed by the commentary citing Radd al-Muhtar.
The commentary presents Abu Hanifa's view as the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن كان له عمان وخالان فذا لعميه (فإن كان له عمان وخالان ، فذا لعميه ) ، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له ، وقالا : يقسم بينهم أرباعاً لعدم اعتبار الأقربية. ١ ] قوله : فإن كان له عمّان.... الخ ؛ هذا تفريع على قوله : الأقرب فالأقرب ؛ أي إن كان للموصي عمّان وخالان فذا : أي الموصى به لعميه ؛ لأنهما أقرب من الخالين ؛ لأن قرابتهما من جهة الأب، والإنسان ينسب إلى أبيه. ألا ترى أن الولاية للعم دون الخال في النكاح، فثبت أنهما أقرب من طريق الحكم، «اتقاني»، وهذا حيث كان الوارث غيرهما ، وكذا يقال فيما بعد، وهو ظاهر. هكذا الرد المحتار).
If he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then (the bequest) is for his two paternal uncles. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is divided among them in fourths, because consideration of priority (aqrabiyya) is not taken. [1] His statement: 'If he has two paternal uncles...' etc. This is a branch on his statement: 'the nearest, then the nearest'; meaning if the testator has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then 'so for his two paternal uncles': meaning the bequest is for his two paternal uncles because they are closer than the maternal uncles; because their relation is from the father's side, and a person is attributed to his father. Do you not see that guardianship in marriage is for the paternal uncle, not the maternal uncle? So it is established that they are closer by way of legal ruling. And this is where there is no other heir. And similarly it is said for what follows. This is apparent. Thus in Radd al-Muhtar.
Source pages p. 621

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the distribution of a bequest to relatives when the testator has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles. Abu Hanifa rules that the entire bequest goes to the two paternal uncles because they are closer in kinship (aqrabiyya). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree, arguing that the bequest should be divided into fourths, each of the four relatives receiving one quarter, as they do not consider relative closeness in bequests. The commentary explains Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the principle is 'the nearest, then the nearest' (al-aqrab fa al-aqrab). Paternal uncles are closer because their relation is through the father, and a person is attributed to his father. Evidence is adduced from guardianship in marriage, where the paternal uncle has priority over the maternal uncle, proving that paternal uncles are legally considered closer. This ruling applies when there are no other heirs. The commentary cites Radd al-Muhtar in support.

Key Terms
الأقرب فالأقرب (al-aqrab fa al-aqrab): The principle of giving priority to the nearest relative in distribution of bequests or inheritance.
الولاية (al-wilayah): Guardianship, specifically in marriage. Evidence that paternal uncle is closer than maternal uncle.
الخال (al-khal): Maternal uncle. In this context, considered less close than paternal uncle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

In Hanafi fiqh, when bequests are made to relatives, paternal uncles take precedence over maternal uncles due to closer lineage, as established by analogy to marriage guardianship.

Wasiyyah Distribution: One Paternal Uncle and Two Maternal Uncles
Intra-Hanafi dispute on division with one uncle and two maternal uncles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dividing a bequest among one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, explain the linguistic basis for Abu Hanifa's position, and distinguish it from the Sahibayn's equal division.

Core Idea
In wasiyyah, a plural wording requires at least two recipients; the closest relative takes half and the next group shares the other half.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute over the distribution of a bequest (wasiyyah) when the testator has one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles. Abu Hanifa rules that the paternal uncle takes half and the maternal uncles share the other half, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue for equal thirds. Understanding the linguistic principle of 'aqall al-jam' (minimum plural) is key to grasping the Hanafi position and its application in bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the dispute
The testator makes a bequest to 'my relatives' (plural). Survivors: one paternal uncle (عم) and two maternal uncles (خالان). The dispute is how to divide the bequest among them.
The case appears in al-Hidayah and al-Zayla‘i.
2
Apply the Hanafi linguistic rule: aqall al-jam'
In wasiyyah, the minimum number for a plural (جمع) is two, not three. So 'relatives' (plural) requires at least two recipients. Here we have three individuals, but the plural condition is satisfied by any two.
This differs from general Arabic grammar where plural usually means three or more.
3
Determine shares via closeness (qarabah)
Among the relatives, the paternal uncle is the closest (أقرب). He therefore takes half (the maximum for a single relative). The remaining half goes to the maternal uncles (the next group), and since they are two, they split that half equally (each gets a quarter).
Abu Hanifa's ruling: paternal uncle = 1/2, each maternal uncle = 1/4.
4
Contrast with the Sahibayn's view
The Sahibayn disregard closeness and divide the bequest equally into thirds: each relative gets 1/3. They do not apply the aqall al-jam' rule in this manner.
Their view is based on a different interpretation of the plural.
5
Understand the tarjih and exception
The commentary (and al-Hidayah) supports Abu Hanifa's view, citing that the wording is plural, so the maternal uncles are joined to the paternal uncle to form a plural, and the uncle's closeness gives him half. An exception: if the bequest wording is singular (e.g., 'to a relative'), then the closest relative takes all.
This exception is from al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي عم وخالين نصف بينه وبينهما؛ لأن أقل الجمع إذا كان اثنين، فللواحد النصف بقي النصف الآخر، فيكون للخاليين، وعندهما: يقسم أثلاثا بينهم. [٢] قوله: وفي عم وخالين... الخ؛ أي إذا أوصى لأقاربه، وترك عماً وخالين فللعم النصف، والنصف الباقي للخالين؛ لأن أقل الجمع... الخ، وقوله: نصف صيغة ماضي، مبني على المفعول من التنصيف والضمير يرجع إلى الموصى له. [٣] قوله: فيكون للخالين؛ لأن اللفظ جمع، فلا بد من اعتبار الجمع فيه وهو الاثنان في الوصية كما مر مراراً، فيضم إلى العم الخالان؛ ليصير جمعاً، فيأخذ العم النصف؛ لأنه أقرب، ويأخذ الخالان النصف الباقي؛ لعدم من تقدم عليه. كذا في الزيلعي. بخلاف ما إذا أوصى لذي قرابة، وللموصي عم وخالان، حيث يكون الكل للعم؛ لأن اللفظ للمفرد، فيحرز الواحد الكل، إذ هو الأقرب. كذا في الهداية.
And in (the case of) one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, half between him and them. Because the least of the plural is two. So for the one (paternal uncle) the half, the other half remains, so it is for the two maternal uncles. And according to the two (Sahibayn): it is divided into thirds among them. [2] His statement: 'And in one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles...' etc.; meaning if he made a bequest to his relatives and left one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle half, and the remaining half for the two maternal uncles; because the least of the plural... etc. And his statement 'half' is a past tense form, passive, from tansif (to halve), and the pronoun refers to the legatee. [3] His statement: 'so it is for the two maternal uncles'; because the wording is plural, so consideration of the plural is necessary, and here in bequest it is two, as has been repeated many times. So the maternal uncles are joined to the paternal uncle to make a plural. So the paternal uncle takes half because he is closer, and the two maternal uncles take the remaining half because there is no one who precedes them. Thus in al-Zayla'i. Contrary to the case where one makes a bequest to a relative, and the testator has a paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, where the whole is for the paternal uncle; because the wording is singular, so the single one takes the whole, because he is the closest. Thus in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 621

Commentary
This passage presents a further case and another intra-Hanafi dispute. When the testator has one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, Abu Hanifa rules: the paternal uncle gets half, and the two maternal uncles share the other half (each getting one quarter). The reasoning: the wording of the bequest is 'to my relatives,' which is a plural. The minimum plural in bequests is two (as established earlier). Here we have three relatives: one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles. To satisfy the plural, we need at least two recipients. Since the paternal uncle is the closest, he takes half. The remaining half goes to the two maternal uncles because they are the next closest, and the plural condition is fulfilled by them collectively. The Sahibayn, however, say it should be divided into three equal parts (each gets one third), because they do not prioritize closeness. The commentary then clarifies the linguistic reasoning and distinguishes the case where the bequest is worded 'to a relative' (singular), in which case the single closest relative (the paternal uncle) takes the entire bequest.

Key Terms
أقل الجمع (aqall al-jam'): The minimum number that constitutes a plural; in wasiyyah it is two.
اللفظ جمع (al-lafz jam'): The wording is in plural form, necessitating at least two recipients.
التنصيف (al-tansif): Halving; the act of dividing into two equal parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a bequest to relatives when there is one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, according to Abu Hanifa, what share do the maternal uncles receive?
A) One third each
B) One quarter each
C) One half each
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi wasiyyah, a plural wording requires at least two recipients, and the closest relative takes half, with the remainder going to the next group.

Three Rulings on Bequest Distribution: Single Uncle, Aunt, and Children
Three Hanafi rulings on bequest distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for bequests to a single paternal uncle, the equality of uncle and aunt, and the equality of male and female children, and explain the linguistic reasoning behind the single uncle's half share.

Core Idea
In Hanafi bequest law, a single uncle gets half, aunt equals uncle, and children share equally regardless of gender.

This lesson examines three specific distribution rules from the Hanafi school regarding bequests to relatives. The first rule determines the share of a single paternal uncle when the bequest is to 'relatives' (aqarib). The second establishes equality between paternal uncle and aunt. The third mandates equal division among male and female children when the bequest is to 'children'. These rulings illustrate how linguistic principles and the minimum of plural guide bequest distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage covers three distinct rulings: (1) bequest to relatives with only one paternal uncle, (2) bequest to relatives with both a paternal uncle and aunt, (3) bequest to 'children of Zayd'.
Each ruling is a separate rule of distribution.
2
First ruling: single uncle's share
When a testator bequeaths to his relatives and has only one paternal uncle, the uncle takes half of the bequest; the other half is returned to the legal heirs because there is no other eligible relative. The reasoning is that the word 'relatives' is plural, and the minimum plural for bequests is two. Thus we treat the absence of a second relative as if there were one, so the uncle is one of two and gets half.
This is based on linguistic necessity, not qiyas.
3
Examine the objection and Hanafi response
An objector argues by qiyas: if there were more uncles, each would get a smaller share, so a single uncle should get less than half (e.g., one-third). The Hanafi response: the analogy fails because the plural minimum is a fixed linguistic rule; we cannot apply proportional qiyas here. The minimum is two, so the share is half.
The response emphasizes the primacy of linguistic principles over analogical reasoning.
4
Second ruling: uncle and aunt equal
If the testator has both a paternal uncle and a paternal aunt, they share the bequest equally. This holds even though the aunt is not a Quranic heir; she is still entitled to the bequest due to kinship, just as a slave or non-Muslim relative would be.
Equality based on equal kinship, not inheritance categorisation.
5
Third ruling: male and female children equal
If the bequest is to 'the children of Zayd', male and female share equally in division and entitlement. The term 'children' (walad) includes all equally, unlike inheritance where males get double.
This is a key difference between bequest and inheritance rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي عم له نصف : أي أوصى للأقارب، وله عم واحد له النصفُ لما ذكرنا آنفا . والعم والعمة سواء فيها. وفي ولد زيد الذكر والأنثى سواء. [١] قوله : وفي عمّ له نصف ؛ أي فيما إذا أوصى للأقارب، وله عم واحد فللعم نصف الوصية، ويرد النصف على الورثة ؛ لعدم مَن يستحقه ؛ لأنَّ اللفظ جمع، وأدناه في الوصيّة الاثنان فيكون لكلِّ واحدٍ منهما النصف ؛ فلذا يعطى له النصف، والنصف الآخر يرد على الورثة. كذا في «الزَّيْلَعِي» واعترض بأنّ في هذا جعل عدم المزاحم بمنزلة وجودِ المزاحم، حيث قيل : إذا كان معه عم آخر كان له النصف، فكذا إذا لم يكن معه عمّ آخر كان له النصف، فكان القائل أن يقول : إذا كان له عمّ واحد كان له الثلث ؛ لأنه إذا كان معه عمان كان له الثلث، فكذا إذا لم يكن معه غيره، وعلى هذا يقال : يجب له الربع أو الخمس عند انفراده قياساً على تقدير أن يكون معه ثلاثة أو أربعة أعمام. وأجيب بأن ذلك غير لازم ؛ لأنَّ اعتبار المجموع كلها ساقطة ؛ لتعذره، فتعين أدنى ما يستعمل فيه وهو الاثنان ؛ لتيقنه ، والعم الواحد نصف الاثنين، فيكون له نصف مالها، فإذا أخذ العم النصف صار كأن لم يكن، فيكون الباقي للورثة. هكذا في «العناية») [۲] قوله : والعم والعمة سواء ؛ أي إن أوصى لأقاربه وله عم وعمّةٌ فهما سواء في الوصية ؛ أي يقسم الموصى به بينهما على السوية ؛ لاستواء قرابتهما، والعمة وإن لم تكن وارثة فهي مستحقة للوصية كما لو كان القريب رقيقاً أو كافراً. كذا في «الهداية». [٣] قوله : وفي ولد زيد... الخ ؛ أي إن أوصى لولدِ زيد، فالوصية بينهم، والذكر والأنثى فيه سواء في القسمة والاستحقاق ؛ لأنَّ اسم الولد ينتظم الكل انتظاماً واحداً.
And (in the case of) one paternal uncle, for him half. i.e., He made a bequest to relatives and he has one paternal uncle: for him half, as we mentioned above. And the paternal uncle and paternal aunt are equal in it. And in 'children of Zayd', male and female are equal. [1] His statement: 'And in one paternal uncle, for him half'; i.e., when he makes a bequest to relatives and he has one paternal uncle, then for the paternal uncle half of the bequest, and the half is returned to the heirs because there is no one who deserves it; because the wording is plural, and its least in bequest is two, so each would get half; therefore he is given half, and the other half is returned to the heirs. Thus in al-Zayla'i. And an objection was raised that this makes the absence of a competitor equivalent to the presence of a competitor, because it is said: if there was another uncle with him, he would get half; likewise if there is no other uncle, he gets half. So one might say: if he had one uncle, he should get one-third; because if there were two uncles with him, he would get one-third? Actually the objection is: if he had one uncle, he should get one-third; because if there were two uncles with him, he would get one-third? The text seems corrupt; but the general meaning is that the objector argues by qiyas: if the number of uncles increases, the share of each decreases, so when alone, the share should be smaller. The response: this analogy is not valid because we are forced to consider the minimum plural (two). The single uncle is treated as one of two, so he takes half. [2] His statement: 'And the paternal uncle and paternal aunt are equal'; i.e., if he makes a bequest to his relatives and he has a paternal uncle and a paternal aunt, they are equal in the bequest; i.e., the bequest is divided equally between them because their kinship is equal. And the paternal aunt, even though she is not an heir, is still entitled to the bequest, just as if the relative were a slave or a disbeliever. Thus in al-Hidayah. [3] His statement: 'And in the children of Zayd...' etc.; i.e., if he makes a bequest to the children of Zayd, the bequest is among them, and male and female are equal in division and entitlement, because the term 'children' includes all equally.
Source pages p. 622

Commentary
This passage contains three distinct rulings from the matn with commentary. First, if the testator bequeaths to his relatives and has only one paternal uncle, the uncle gets half of the bequest; the other half is returned to the legal heirs (because there is no other eligible relative). The reasoning: the bequest wording is plural ('relatives'), and the minimum for a plural in bequests is two. So we must treat the absence of another relative as if there is one. An objection is raised that this treats absence of a competitor like presence, and by analogy, the share should decrease as competitors increase, so a single uncle should get less than half. The response: the analogy fails because the requirement of a plural is a linguistic necessity; we must assume the minimum (two). The uncle, being one of two, takes half. Once he takes half, the remaining half is returned to the heirs. The second ruling: paternal uncle and paternal aunt are equal in the bequest. Even though the aunt is not a Quranic heir (paternal aunt is a non-heir in Hanafi faraid), she is still entitled to the bequest, analogous to a relative who is a slave or non-Muslim. The third ruling: if the bequest is to 'the children of Zayd', male and female are equal in division and entitlement, because the term 'children' (walad) includes all equally, unlike inheritance where males get double.

Key Terms
الرد على الورثة (al-radd 'ala al-warathah): The return of the unclaimed portion of the bequest to the testator's legal heirs.
السوية (al-sawiyyah): Equality in division; equal shares.
الولد (al-walad): Child; in bequests, includes male and female equally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Entire bequest goes to the uncle
B) Half goes to the uncle and half is returned to the legal heirs
C) The uncle gets nothing
D) The bequest is void

Key Takeaway
Hanafi bequest distribution rules emphasize linguistic precision (minimum plural leads to half share) and equality of male and female children, distinct from inheritance.

Bequest to Relatives: One Uncle Gets Half
Commentary expanding a ruling on bequest distribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the minimum plural in a will is two to determine the share of a single relative.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'relatives' is split as if two existed; one uncle takes half, the rest returns to heirs.

When a person makes a will benefiting his relatives using a plural term, but only one relative survives, how much does he receive? The Hanafi school resolves this using a linguistic principle: the minimum of a plural in the context of a will is two. This lesson unpacks the reasoning from al-Zayla'i and al-Inayah, including an objection and its rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
The deceased bequeathed to his 'relatives' (plural). Only one paternal uncle qualifies. What share does the uncle receive?
The key is interpreting the plural word in the will.
2
Locate the primary proof
The Hanafi proof is the linguistic rule that the minimum meaning of a plural in a will is two, not three. This is based on certainty: since the word could refer to two or more, the certain minimum is two.
This differs from other contexts where plural might mean three.
3
Analyze the qiyas
The ruling for one uncle is derived by analogy to two uncles. If two existed, each would get half. Therefore, the one uncle takes the half that would belong to one of the two.
The illa is that the plural is taken at its minimum, two.
4
Understand the objection
Some scholars object: if two uncles each get half, shouldn't one uncle get a third by analogy to three uncles (where each gets a third)? They argue consistency would require reducing the share as the number of possible relatives increases.
This objection uses a different analogy based on three as the plural minimum.
5
See the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that three is not certain; only two is certain. The minimum plural (two) is adopted due to certainty. One uncle is half of two, so he gets half.
The response prioritizes certainty over speculative analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وفي عمّ له نصف ؛ أي فيما إذا أوصى للأقارب، وله عم واحد فللعم نصف الوصية، النصف يرد على الورثة ; لعدم مَن يستحقه ; لأنَّ اللفظ جمع، وأدناه في الوصيّة الاثنان فيكون لكلِّ واحدٍ منهما النصف ; فلذا يعطى له النصف، والنصف الآخر يرد على الورثة. كذا في «الزَّيْلَعِي»(1) واعترض بأنّ في هذا جعل عدم المزاحم بمنزلة وجودِ المزاحم، حيث قيل : إذا كان معه عم آخر كان له النصف، فكذا إذا لم يكن معه عمّ آخر كان له النصف، فكان القائل أن يقول : إذا كان له عمّ واحد كان له الثلث ; لأنه إذا كان معه عمان كان له الثلث، فكذا إذا لم يكن معه غيره، وعلى هذا يقال : يجب له الربع أو الخمس عند انفراده قياساً على تقدير أن يكون معه ثلاثة أو أربعة أعمام. وأجيب بأن ذلك غير لازم ; لأنَّ اعتبار المجموع كلها ساقطة ; لتعذره، فتعين أدنى ما يستعمل فيه وهو الاثنان ; لتيقنه ، والعم الواحد نصف الاثنين، فيكون له نصف مالها، فإذا أخذ العم النصف صار كأن لم يكن، فيكون الباقي للورثة. هكذا في «العناية»(2)
His saying: 'And for an uncle he has half' means when he bequeaths to relatives, and he has one uncle, then for the uncle is half the will, and the half is returned to the heirs due to there being no one who deserves it, because the word (جمع) is plural, and the minimum in a will is two, so each of them would have half. Therefore he is given half, and the other half is returned to the heirs. Thus in al-Zayla'i. And it was objected that in this, the absence of a rival is made like the existence of a rival, since it was said: if he has another uncle he has half, so likewise if he does not have another uncle he has half. So the proponent should say: if he has one uncle he has a third, because if he has two uncles he has a third, so likewise if he does not have another. And based on this it is said: he must get a quarter or fifth when alone, by analogy to if he had three or four uncles. And it was answered that this is not necessary because considering the whole (as plural) is impossible, so the minimum used, which is two, is determined due to certainty. And one uncle is half of two, so he takes half of the bequest, and when the uncle takes half, it is as if he did not exist, so the remainder is for the heirs. Thus in al-Inayah.
Source pages p. 622

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on a ruling from the matn of al-Wiqaya. It addresses a bequest to relatives (الأقارب) when there is only one paternal uncle (عم). The ruling: the uncle receives half the bequest, and the other half is returned to the heirs. The reasoning is based on the legal principle that the word for 'relatives' is a plural, and the minimum number for a plural in the context of a will is two. If there were two uncles, each would get half; since there is only one, he gets the half that would belong to one of the two, and the other half goes back to the heirs. The text then presents an objection: if there were two uncles, each gets half, so by the same logic, if there is one uncle, he should get the third (because if there were three uncles each would get a third). The objection attempts a proportional analogy. The response is that considering the full plural (three or more) is impossible here because the context of a will requires certainty, so the minimum (two) is used. Thus, the single uncle is treated as half of the minimum plural, giving him half. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position as recorded in al-Zayla'i and al-Inayah.

Key Terms
عم (amm): Paternal uncle
جمع (jam'): Plural form of a word in Arabic grammar
وصية (wasiyyah): Bequest or will

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person bequeaths to his 'relatives' and has only one paternal uncle, what portion does the uncle receive?
A) All of the bequest
B) Half of the bequest
C) One-third of the bequest
D) One-quarter of the bequest

Key Takeaway
When a will uses a plural term for relatives, the Hanafi school interprets the minimum as two, so a single relative receives half of the bequeathed amount.

Equality of Uncle and Aunt in a Bequest to Relatives
Clarifying equality of uncle and aunt in a bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that in a bequest to relatives, the uncle and aunt receive equal shares and explain the rationale based on equality of relationship.

Core Idea
In a bequest to relatives, uncle and aunt are equal — relation, not inheritance status, determines the share.

This short passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies a key point in the Hanafi law of bequests (wasiyyah). When a testator makes a will in favour of his relatives, the distribution is based on closeness of relationship, not on whether the relative is an heir in the inheritance system. Thus, a paternal aunt, who is not a Quranic heir, receives equally with a paternal uncle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the operative scenario
The text assumes a bequest made to 'relatives' (aqarib) without specifying individuals. The question arises whether all relatives share equally or according to inheritance shares.
This is a common issue in drafting wills.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on uncle and aunt
Both receive equal shares because their relationship to the testator is equally close — both are children of the testator's father.
The text explicitly says 'فهما سواء'.
3
Extract the underlying principle
The criterion is equality of relationship, not inheritance capacity. The aunt is not a Quranic heir but still receives her share. This is analogous to a slave or non-Muslim relative, who also can receive a bequest.
This shows that wasiyyah is a voluntary transfer, not bound by faraid rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والعم والعمة سواء ; أي إن أوصى لأقاربه وله عم وعمّةٌ فهما سواء في الوصية ; أي يقسم الموصى به بينهما على السوية ; لاستواء قرابتهما، والعمة وإن لم تكن وارثة فهي مستحقة للوصية كما لو كان القريب رقيقاً أو كافراً. كذا في «الهداية(3)»
His saying: 'And the uncle and aunt are equal' means if he bequeaths to his relatives and he has an uncle and an aunt, they are equal in the bequest; i.e., the bequeathed item is divided equally between them due to the equality of their relationship. And the aunt, even if she is not an heir, is entitled to the bequest, just as if the relative were a slave or a disbeliever. Thus in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 622

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling that when a bequest is made to relatives (أقاربه) and there are specific individuals like an uncle (عم) and an aunt (عمة), they share equally in the bequest. The reason is that both are equally related to the testator. Though the aunt might not inherit in the faraid system (as she is not a designated heir in many cases), she is still entitled to a bequest because the will is a voluntary act of charity. The commentary draws a parallel to cases where the recipient is a slave or a non-Muslim — they can receive a bequest. This is the position recorded in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
عمة (ammah): Paternal aunt
سوية (sawiyyah): Equality, equal shares

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths to his relatives and has a paternal uncle and a paternal aunt, how is the bequest divided between them?
A) The uncle gets double the aunt
B) They get equal shares
C) Only the uncle gets a share
D) The aunt gets half of the uncle's share

Key Takeaway
In a bequest to relatives, uncle and aunt receive equal shares because they are equally related, regardless of inheritance status.

Bequest to 'Walad': Equal Division Among Male and Female Children
Ruling on equal division in bequest to children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a bequest to 'walad' includes all children equally regardless of gender, and distinguish the case of a sole child from a bequest to 'awlad'.

Core Idea
The term 'walad' in a bequest includes all children equally, male and female alike.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi wasiyyah law: how to interpret a bequest made to the 'child' or 'children' of a named person. The Arabic term 'walad' can be ambiguous, but the Hanafi school has settled that it covers both male and female offspring equally. We will also explore an important distinction between using the singular collective 'walad' and the plural 'awlad' when the beneficiary has only one child.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest wording
First, note that the bequest is to 'walad Zayd' (the child/children of Zaid). The term 'walad' is a singular noun used collectively.
Do not assume it means only one child; it can refer to multiple offspring.
2
Determine inclusion of both genders
Recognize that 'walad' encompasses both male and female. The passage states it applies 'uniformly' (intiẓāman wāḥidan) to all children.
This is a linguistic ruling specific to Hanafi fiqh.
3
Apply equal division
When there are multiple children (mixed genders or all female), divide the bequest equally among them. No child is preferred.
This differs from inheritance (farā'id), where males often receive double.
4
Handle the sole child exception
If Zaid has only one child, that child takes the entire bequest. The passage explicitly states: 'if he has only one child, the entire bequest is for that one'.
Contrast with the rule for 'awlad' (plural) where a single child gets half.
5
Contrast with 'awlad' (plural)
If the bequest is to 'awlad fulan' (children of so-and-so) and there is only one child, that child receives half, not the whole. The distinction is explained in al-Kifayah: 'walad' is a singular collective that includes all, while 'awlad' is a proper plural requiring at least two.
This is a subtle point that can change the outcome entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وفي ولد زيد... الخ ; أي إن أوصى لولدِ زيد، فالوصية بينهم، والذكر والأنثى فيه سواء في القسمة والاستحقاق ; لأنَّ اسم الولد ينتظم الكل انتظاماً واحداً، حتى لو كانوا ذكورا وإناثا يقسم بينهم بالسوية. ولو كان الكل إناثاً دخلن تحت الوصية ; لأنَّ الوصية حصلت باسم الولد، واسم الولد يطلق على الإناث حالة الانفراد، وكما يطلق على الذكور، ثمّ في مسألتنا إن لم يكن له إلا ولد واحدٌ كان الموصى به كله له ، بخلاف ما لو أوصى لأولاد فلان وله ولد واحد، فإنه يستحق النصف، ووجه الفرق مذكور في «الكفاية»)1]
His saying: 'And regarding the child of Zaid... etc.' means if he bequeaths to the child (walad) of Zaid, then the bequest is among them, and the male and female are equal in division and entitlement because the term 'al-walad' encompasses all in one uniform manner. So if they are males and females, it is divided equally among them. And if all are females, they are included in the bequest because the bequest was made using the term 'walad', and the term 'walad' applies to females when alone, just as it applies to males. Then, in our case, if he has only one child, the entire bequest is for that one, unlike if he bequeaths to the children (awlad) of so-and-so and has one child, then he gets half. The distinction is mentioned in al-Kifayah.
Source pages p. 622

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling for a bequest to 'walad Zayd' (the child/children of Zaid). The key point: the word 'walad' (singular child, but also used collectively for offspring) includes both male and female equally. Thus, if there are multiple children, they share the bequest equally regardless of gender. Even if all are females, they all receive shares because 'walad' applies to females in isolation as well. A special case: if there is only one child, that child gets the entire bequest. This differs from a bequest to 'awlad' (plural of walad) where, if there is only one child, he/she gets half. The distinction is explained in al-Kifayah: 'walad' as a singular collective noun includes all, while 'awlad' as a proper plural may require a minimum of two.

Key Terms
ولد (walad): Child/offspring, singular form used collectively
أولاد (awlad): Plural of walad, meaning children

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a testator bequeaths to 'walad Zayd' and Zayd has only one child, what does that child receive?
A) The entire bequest
B) Half the bequest
C) Nothing
D) It depends on the child's gender

Key Takeaway
The term 'walad' in a bequest includes all children equally, and a sole child takes the entire bequest.

Bequest to Heirs: Male Gets Share of Two Females
Ruling statement with a condition from al-Kifayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for a bequest made to 'heirs' and identify the condition for its validity.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'heirs' follows inheritance shares: male gets double female, provided heirs survive testator.

This lesson examines a specific wasiyyah scenario: a testator bequeaths to 'the heirs of Zaid'. The Hanafi ruling is that the distribution mirrors inheritance law (faraid), where a male gets twice a female's share. A critical condition from al-Kifayah is introduced: the bequest is only valid if the intended heirs are alive at the testator's death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the bequest
The bequest is made to 'the heirs of Zaid' – a general term covering all legal heirs (male and female).
2
State the distribution ruling
The bequest is divided among them such that a male gets twice the share of a female.
3
Explain the reasoning
The term 'heirs' (ورثة) indicates the testator intended differentiation as in inheritance (faraid).
Hanafi law presumes that the word 'heirs' calls to mind the inheritance shares.
4
Apply the condition from al-Kifayah
For the bequest to be valid, the intended recipients (the heirs of Zaid) must survive the testator. If they die before him, the bequest is void.
This condition is stated in al-Kifayah and is relied upon in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وفي ورثته... الخ ; أي إذا أوصى لورثة زيدٍ فالوصية بينهم، للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين; لأنه لما نص على لفظ الورثة آذن ذلك بأن قصده التفضيل كما في الميراث. قال في «الكفاية» (3): هذا إذا مات الموصي لورثته ، ثم مات الموصي ، أما إذا مات الموصي قبل أن يموت الموصى لورثته فالوصية باطلة.
His saying: 'And regarding his heirs... etc.' means if he bequeaths to the heirs of Zaid, then the bequest is among them, for the male the share of two females, because when he specifically used the term 'heirs', it indicates that his intention was differentiation as in inheritance. Al-Kifayah says: This applies if the testator dies for his heirs (i.e., the heirs are alive at the testator's death), then the testator dies. If the testator dies before the person bequeathed to his heirs dies, the bequest is void.
Source pages p. 623

Commentary
This passage deals with a bequest to 'the heirs of Zaid'. The ruling: the distribution follows the inheritance shares (faraid) where a male gets twice the share of a female. The reason is that the term 'heirs' (ورثة) evokes the law of inheritance which differentiates based on gender. The commentary adds a condition from al-Kifayah: for this bequest to be valid, the intended recipients (the heirs of Zaid) must survive the testator. If the testator dies before them (meaning the heirs of Zaid die before the testator), the bequest becomes void because it can only take effect on those who are alive at the testator's death.

Key Terms
ورثة (warathah): Heirs, those entitled to inherit

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths to 'the heirs of Zaid' and Zaid has a son and a daughter, how is the bequest divided?
A) Equally between son and daughter
B) Son gets two-thirds, daughter one-third
C) Son gets twice the daughter
D) Only the son gets the bequest

Key Takeaway
A bequest to 'heirs' is distributed according to faraid (male:female = 2:1) provided the heirs survive the testator.

Bequest to countable vs uncountable groups: the rule of enumeration
Ruling on bequest to specific groups like orphans, blind, etc.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for bequests to specific groups and apply the condition of enumeration (ihsa') to determine who receives the bequest.

Core Idea
A bequest to a group that can be counted includes all members; if uncountable, only the poor benefit.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies a key principle in wills: when a testator leaves a bequest to a specific category of people (orphans, blind, etc.), the outcome depends on whether the group can be enumerated. If it can, each member receives a share; if not, the bequest is channeled to the needy among them, aligning with the charitable purpose of the will. The commentary also provides a precise legal definition of 'orphan' using the prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the testator has named a specific group (e.g., 'orphans of the sons of so-and-so', 'the blind', 'the paralyzed', 'widows'). This is not a bequest to individuals by name, but to a class.
2
Check enumerability (ihsa')
Determine whether the group can be precisely counted. If it is a small, finite group, it is countable; if it is large and indefinite (e.g., all orphans of a large tribe), it is not countable.
The passage says 'if they are a people who can be counted' (إن كانوا قوما يحصون).
3
Apply the ruling based on enumeration
If countable, every member—poor and rich, male and female—receives a share. If not countable, only the poor among them receive.
Reason: When countable, actual possession (tamlik) is possible; when not, the charitable purpose (qurbah) dictates that the needy be prioritized.
4
Understand the rationale
The bequest is a transfer of ownership (tamlik). If the group is uncountable, it is impossible to give each member individually, so the bequest is interpreted as a charitable offering to the needy, fulfilling the testator's intent of seeking closeness to Allah.
5
Define 'orphan' (yatim)
Note the legal definition: a child whose father has died, and this status ends at puberty, based on the hadith 'There is no orphanhood after puberty.' This restricts the term to minors.
This definition affects who qualifies as an orphan in the bequest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وفي أيتام بنيه ; أي لو أوصى لأيتام بني فلان أو لعميانهم أو لزمناهم أو لأراملهم إن كانوا قوما يحصون دخل في الوصية فقيرهم وغنّيهم، ذكورهم وإناثهم ; لأنه أمكن تحقيق التمليك في حقهم، والوصية تمليك وإلا أي وإن كانوا لا يحصلون، فالوصية في الفقراء منهم ; لأنَّ المقصود من الوصيّة القربة، وهي في سدّ الحاجة، وردّ الجوعة، وهذه الأسامي تشعر بتحقيق الحاجة، فجاز حمله على الفقراء (3). اعلم أن الأيتام جمع يتيم : وهو اسم لصغير مات أبوه ; لقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لا يتم بعد الحلم».
His saying: 'And regarding the orphans of his sons...' means if he bequeaths to the orphans of the sons of so-and-so, or to their blind, or to their paralyzed, or to their widows, if they are a people who can be counted, then both the poor and the rich among them, males and females, are included in the bequest because it is possible to effect possession in their favor, and the bequest is possession. Otherwise, if they cannot be counted, then the bequest is for the poor among them because the purpose of the bequest is closeness (to Allah), and that is fulfilled by fulfilling needs and alleviating hunger, and these names indicate the realization of need, so it is permissible to interpret it as (meaning) the poor. Know that 'orphans' is the plural of 'orphan', which is a name for a minor whose father has died, due to the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'No orphanhood after puberty.'
Source pages p. 623

Commentary
This passage rules on a bequest made to specific groups: orphans (أيتام), blind (عميان), paralyzed (زمنى), or widows (أرامل) of a certain lineage (e.g., sons of so-and-so). The key condition is whether the group can be enumerated (يحصون). If they can be counted, all members—poor and rich, male and female—receive shares equally because the bequest is a transfer of ownership (تمليك) and it's possible to give each. If they cannot be counted (i.e., a large, unenumerable group), then only the poor among them receive, because the underlying purpose of a bequest is charity (قربة), which is best served by alleviating need. The commentary then defines the term 'يتيم' (orphan) using the prophetic hadith: 'There is no orphanhood after puberty.' This establishes the legal definition: an orphan is a minor who has lost his father.

Key Terms
يتيم (yatim): Orphan: a minor whose father has died
قربة (qurbah): An act of drawing closer to Allah, i.e., a meritorious deed
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership; the legal effect of a bequest
إحصاء (ihsa'): Enumeration; the ability to count individuals in a group

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man bequeaths to 'the blind of the sons of Zaid' and there are 50 blind people but they cannot be precisely counted, who receives the bequest?
A) Only the rich among them
B) Only the poor among them
C) All of them equally
D) The bequest is void

Key Takeaway
The enumerability of the group determines the distribution of a bequest: if countable, all members share; if not, only the needy receive.

Bequest to Heirs: Distribution According to Inheritance Shares
Ruling on bequest to heirs with distribution like inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a bequest to 'heirs' is distributed according to inheritance shares and identify the condition for its validity.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'heirs' follows inheritance shares; the testator must outlive the named person for the bequest to be valid.

When someone makes a bequest to 'the heirs of Zayd', how should that bequest be divided? The Hanafi school holds that the word 'heirs' implies the distribution rules of inheritance, not equal division. However, there is a crucial condition: the testator must die after the person whose heirs are named. This lesson examines the ruling and its rationale from the classical texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses a bequest (wasiyyah) made to the heirs of a specific person (e.g., 'the heirs of Zayd'). The ruling is that the bequest is valid and distributed among those heirs according to inheritance shares: a male heir receives twice the share of a female heir.
The core ruling is from the matn, and the commentary clarifies the reasoning.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is linguistic: the word 'heirs' (ورثة) itself indicates the intent to follow inheritance distribution. The commentator states that specifying the word 'heirs' signifies preference as in inheritance.
This is a talil (reasoning) based on the connotation of the term, not an explicit textual source.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
The word 'heirs' is a term that inherently carries the meaning of inheritance and its rules. When a testator uses this term, it shows the intention to adopt the inheritance scheme, including the male-to-female ratio.
Hanafi usul: 'Al-ibrah li al-umum al-lafzi' – the general word is taken in its full meaning.
4
Identify the condition for validity
The passage from al-Kifayah adds a condition: the testator must die after the person whose heirs are named. If the testator dies first, the bequest is invalid (batil) because the intended beneficiaries (the heirs) are not identified at the time of the testator's death.
This condition is essential for the existence of the subject of the bequest.
5
State the practical outcome
In practice, the executor must first check the order of deaths. If the named person dies first, the bequest is distributed among his/her heirs with male:female = 2:1. If the testator dies first, the bequest fails and the property returns to the testator's own heirs.
This distinction prevents misapplication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي ورثته ذكر كأنثيين)؛ لأنه اعتبر الوراثة، وحكم الإرث هذا. [1] قوله : وفي ورثته... الخ أي إذا أوصى لورثة زيدٍ فالوصية بينهم، للذكر مثل حظ الأنثيين؛ لأنه لما نص على لفظ الورثة آذن ذلك بأن قصده التفضيل كما في الميراث. (1) قال في «الكفاية» (۳) : هذا إذا مات الموصي لورثته ، ثم مات الموصي ، أما إذا مات الموصي قبل أن يموت الموصى لورثته فالوصية باطلة.
And in his heirs, the male is like two females, because he considered inheritance, and the ruling of inheritance is this. [1] His statement: 'And in his heirs... etc.' means that if one makes a bequest to the heirs of Zayd, the bequest is divided among them, for the male the share of two females; because when he specified the word 'heirs', it indicates that his intent is preference as in inheritance. (1) He said in al-Kifayah: This is when the testator (the one who made the bequest) dies to his heirs, then the testator dies. But if the testator dies before the one to whom the bequest is made dies, the bequest is invalid.
Source pages p. 623

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the matn and its commentary. The ruling: if someone makes a bequest to the heirs of a person (e.g., 'my bequest to the heirs of Zayd'), the bequest is distributed among them according to the rules of inheritance: a male heir receives twice the share of a female heir. The reason is that the word 'heirs' (ورثة) inherently carries the meaning of inheritance distribution. The commentator adds a condition from al-Kifayah: this ruling applies only if the testator (the one making the bequest) dies after the person whose heirs are named dies. If the testator dies first, the bequest is invalid because the subject of the bequest (the heirs) did not exist as potential recipients at the time of the testator's death.

Key Terms
ورثة (warathah): Heirs of a deceased person, used here to mean the potential inheritors of a specific individual named in the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone makes a bequest to 'the heirs of Zayd', how is the bequest divided among Zayd's heirs according to the Hanafi school?
A) Equally among all heirs
B) According to inheritance shares: male gets twice female
C) Only to the poor among them
D) Only to the male heirs

Key Takeaway
A bequest to 'heirs' is distributed according to inheritance shares (male:female 2:1) only if the testator dies after the named person; otherwise it is invalid.
